Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Introducing Bahr Ulum: A Commentary on Logic
Title page of Bahr Ulum commentary on logic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of a classical Islamic logic commentary from its title page.

Core Idea
A title page is a historical fingerprint of a scholarly work.

Before diving into the content of a classical text, it is essential to understand its provenance. The title page of Bahr Ulum reveals not only the book's subject—logic—but also its scholarly lineage through the commentator, his school, and his creed. This lesson will guide you in reading such front matter critically, so you appreciate the intellectual context in which the author and commentator operated.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text being commented on
Locate the name of the original treatise: 'Milat al-Khalfa' (or 'Sullam al-Khalfa'). This is the foundational work on logic authored by Muhibb Allah al-Bihari. The commentary (sharh) of Bahr Ulum explains this base text.
Remember: the base text is the object of exposition.
2
Identify the commentator and his biographical details
Find the name Abd al-Ali al-Lakhnawi, his birth and death dates (1142-1225 AH / 1729-1810 CE), his affiliation (Hanafi madhhab, Maturidi creed), and his title (Abu al-Abbas). These details situate him in time and scholarly tradition.
Biographical data helps assess the commentator's perspective and authority.
3
Note the original author and his scholarly status
The base text author is Muhibb Allah al-Bihari, who also wrote 'Muslim al-Thubut' (a famous usul al-fiqh text). His death date (1119 AH) and the invocation 'may Allah have mercy on him' indicate he is considered a respected scholar.
Knowing the author's other works gives clues about his expertise.
4
Recognize the modern scholarly apparatus
The title page also gives the editor (Abd al-Qayyum al-Malibari) and publisher (Dar al-Saba). This tells you that the text has been critically edited and is part of a modern publication stream.
Modern editions often include additional notes and corrections.
5
Reflect on the significance of the title page
This single page connects you to centuries of Islamic scholarship: a base text from the 18th-century Indian subcontinent, a commentary from the same region, and a modern critical edition. The chain of transmission (isnad) of knowledge is thus partially visible.
Such front matter is a condensed scholarly biography.

Commentary
This passage is the title page of the book 'Bahr Ulum', which is a commentary (sharh) by Abd al-Ali al-Lakhnawi on a logic text called 'Milat al-Khalfa' (or 'Sullam al-Khalfa') written by Muhibb Allah al-Bihari. The title page provides the name of the commentator, his lineage, his school (Hanafi) and creed (Maturidi), his birth and death dates, and the name of the original author. It also mentions the modern editor and publisher. This front matter introduces the work and its place in the Islamic logical tradition.

Key Takeaway
A title page provides essential clues about the scholarly context, including the base text, commentator, school, creed, and transmission chain of a classical Islamic work.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Introduction and Front Matter

Identifying a Title Page in Islamic Logic
Title page identifying the commentary and its author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract the author, commentator, and key dates from a title page of a classical logic text.

Core Idea
A title page is a scholarly isnad in miniature.

When you open a classical Islamic work, the title page is your first guide. It tells you the name of the book, who wrote it, who commented on it, and when. For the student of logic, this information is essential to situate the text within the scholarly tradition. In this lesson, we examine the title page of Sharh Bahr al-'Ulum, a commentary on Sullam al-'Ulum.

Guided Path
1
Find the main title and subtitle
Locate the primary name of the work (Sharh Bahr al-'Ulum) and any descriptive phrases that follow (e.g., 'on the science of logic').
The subtitle often specifies the subject matter.
2
Identify the commentator and the original author
Note the name of the commentator (al-Karanawi) and the original author of the base text (al-Bahari). The structure is 'Commentary of X on Y by Z'.
Do not confuse the two roles.
3
Extract the biographical dates
Look for both hijri and Gregorian dates. They confirm the historical period of the authors and help you place the work in the intellectual timeline.
Dates are often given in parentheses after the name.

Commentary
This passage is the title page of the book. It identifies the commentary (Sharh Bahr al-'Ulum) and its author (Abu al-'Ayyash 'Abd al-'Ali al-Karanawi), who wrote it on the text Sullam al-'Ulum in the science of logic. The original author is Imam Yuhab Allah al-Bahari, known for his work Muslim al-Thubut in usul al-fiqh. The dates are given in both hijri and gregorian.

Key Takeaway
The title page provides the scholarly chain (isnad) of the text, essential for situating the work in the Islamic logical tradition.

?
Look up the title page of another classical Islamic text you have studied (e.g., al-Hidayah or al-Muwatta). Write down the commentator, the original author, and the date of composition.
?
Explain why knowing the author's full name and scholarly lineage (nisba) helps you evaluate the authority of the work.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Introducing Bahr al-'Ulum and Its Author
Title page presenting the commentary Bahr al-'Ulum on Sullam al-'Ulum and biographical details.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and base text of the commentary Bahr al-'Ulum and situate it within the Hanafi-Maturidi tradition of Islamic logic.

Core Idea
Bahr al-'Ulum is the 'Sea of Sciences' that unlocks the ladder of logic for the Indian Hanafi-Maturidi tradition.

This lesson introduces the commentary Bahr al-'Ulum and its author 'Abd al-'Ali al-Karahnewi, a key figure in the Indian Hanafi-Maturidi school. Understanding the context of this work helps us appreciate how Islamic logic was transmitted and taught in South Asia. The passage also includes blessings and a caution about misattributed sayings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the commentary and its author
Locate the phrase 'شرح بحر العلوم' and note the full name of the commentator: 'عبد العلي بن نظام الدين الكرهنوي المدراسي الجنفي الماتريدي'. This establishes the work as a commentary (sharh) and its author's scholarly affiliation (Hanafi-Maturidi).
The nisbah 'al-Madrasi' indicates he was based in Madras (Chennai), South India.
2
Identify the base text (matn) and its author
Find 'على سلم العلوم' and the name of the matn author: 'محمد بن عبد الشكور العثماني الجنفي البهاري الهندي'. Note that he also wrote 'مسلم الثبوت' in usul al-fiqh.
Sullam al-'Ulum is a standard introductory text in logic within the Indian tradition.
3
Recognize the scholarly lineage and affiliation
Observe that both authors are Hanafi and from the Indian subcontinent. This places the work within a specific madhhab and geographical tradition, which influences the examples and arguments used in the commentary.
The Maturidi theological affiliation is also significant for later discussions on epistemology.
4
Distinguish the Qur'anic verse and poetic line from hadith
The passage quotes verse 22 of Surah al-Ahzab and a line from al-Busiri's Burdah. The phrase 'وروي عن النبي' introduces a saying that is actually from the Burdah, not a prophetic hadith. Learn to verify such attributions.
This is a common misunderstanding: the Burdah line is often mistaken for a hadith.
5
Understand the purpose of front matter in scholarly works
Front matter typically includes blessings, author credentials, and refutations of distortions. This sets the tone and asserts the orthodoxy of the commentary within the tradition.
Skipping front matter can lead to missing important contextual clues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح بحر العلوم لأبي العياش عبد العلي بن نظام الدين الكرهنوي المدراسي الجنفي الماتريدي على سلم العلوم في علم المنطق للإمام الشيخ يُحب الله بن عبد الشكور العثماني الجنفي البهاري الهندي صاحب مسلم الثبوت رحمه الله. دراسة وتحقيق عبد التنصير احمت الشافعي المليباري ماجستير في العقيدة والفلسفة جامعة الأزهر. دار الضياء للنشر والتوزيع الكويت. ثم قال: وَصَدَقَ اللهُ وَرَسُولُهُ وَمَا زَادَهُمْ إِلَّا إِيمَانًا وَتَسْلِيمًا [الأحزاب: ٢٢]. وَيَحْمِلُ هَذَا الدِّينَ مِنْ كُلِّ خَلَفٍ عُدُولُهُ، يَنْفُونَ عَنْهُ تَحْرِيفَ الْغَالِينَ، وَانْتِحَالَ الْجَاهِلِينَ، وَتَأْوِيلَ الْمُبْطِلِينَ. ورُوي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: لَمْ يَمْتَحِنَّا بِمَا تَعْيَ الْعُقُولُ بِهِ حِرْصًا عَلَيْنَا فَلَمْ نَرْتَبْ وَلَمْ نَهِم. الإمام البوصيري في البردة الشريفة.
Commentary of Bahr al-'Ulum by Abi al-'Ayyash 'Abd al-'Ali ibn Nizam al-Din al-Karahnewi al-Madrasi al-Hanafi al-Maturidi on Sullam al-'Ulum in the science of logic by the Imam, the Shaykh, Mahab Allah (or Yuhabb Allah) ibn 'Abd al-Shakur al-'Uthmani al-Hanafi al-Bihari al-Hindi, author of Muslim al-Thubut, may Allah have mercy on him. Study and verification by 'Abd al-Tansir Ahmad al-Shafi'i al-Malibari, Master in Creed and Philosophy from al-Azhar University. Dar al-Diya' for Publishing and Distribution, Kuwait. Then he said: 'And Allah and His Messenger spoke the truth, and it only increased them in faith and submission.' (Al-Ahzab 33:22). 'This religion will be carried by just ones from every generation, who will remove from it the distortions of the extremists, the false claims of the ignorant, and the interpretations of the wrongdoers.' And it is narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'He did not test us with that which the intellects are incapable of, out of care for us, so we did not doubt and did not become confused.' (Imam al-Busiri in the Noble Burdah).
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is the front matter of the book Bahr al-'Ulum, a commentary on the logical work Sullam al-'Ulum. It begins by identifying the author of the commentary, 'Abd al-'Ali al-Karahnewi, and his lineage, noting his Hanafi-Maturidi affiliation. The original matn (Sullam al-'Ulum) was written by Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Shakur al-Bahari, author of Muslim al-Thubut. The passage also mentions the modern editor and publisher. Following this, a Qur'anic verse from Surah al-Ahzab is quoted, then a well-known pseudo-hadith (often quoted in scholarly works) about the carriers of religious knowledge who protect it from distortion. Finally, a line from Imam al-Busiri's Burdah is cited, invoking divine care. This introduction sets the scholarly context and seeks blessings for the work. The student should note that the original matn is in logic ('ilm al-mantiq), and the commentary aims to explain its contents. The biographical details help place the work within the Hanafi-Maturidi Indian tradition.

Key Terms
بحر العلوم
سلم العلوم
منطق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Imam al-Busiri
D) 'Abd al-Tansir al-Malibari

Key Takeaway
The front matter of a scholarly work reveals its intellectual lineage and should not be skipped, as it provides crucial context for the arguments that follow.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find one other commentary on Sullam al-'Ulum (e.g., by 'Abd al-Hakim Sialkoti) and compare the author's biographical affiliation to that of al-Karahnewi. Write one sentence on how the affiliation might shape the commentary's approach.
?
Identify the Qur'anic verse and the line from al-Busiri's Burdah in the passage. Explain in one sentence why scholars include such quotations in the front matter of logical texts.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Understanding Front Matter in Islamic Scholarship
Author opens with Quranic verse, hadith, and poetic line as front matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three types of citations used in the front matter of Bahr Ulum and explain their rhetorical purpose.

Core Idea
Front matter in Islamic works grounds logical inquiry in revelation and tradition.

The opening of Bahr Ulum sets the stage not with a logical argument but with divine and prophetic authority. This lesson unpacks the Quranic verse, hadith, and poetic line, showing how they frame the entire study. Understanding this front matter is essential for grasping the author's methodological commitments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three citations
Read the passage and list the three distinct types of texts quoted: a Quranic verse, a narration (hadith), and a line of poetry.
The verse is Quran 33:22; the hadith is a well-known tradition about upright scholars; the poetry is from al-Busiri's Burda.
2
Determine the source and context of each
For each citation, note its original source and how it functions in that source. The Quranic verse praises trust in Allah; the hadith describes preservers of religion; the poetry emphasizes that Allah does not burden believers beyond reason.
3
Explain the rhetorical function of each citation
Why did the author choose these specific quotes? The verse establishes divine truthfulness, the hadith highlights scholarly integrity, and the poetry reassures that the study is within rational bounds. Together they create a framework of authority and humility.
4
Synthesize the purpose of the front matter
Summarize how these three elements prepare the reader for a work of logic and theology. They affirm that the study is rooted in revelation, guarded by reliable scholars, and not beyond human reasoning.
This front matter is not part of the logical argument but sets its spiritual and intellectual context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَصَدَقَ اللهُ وَرَسُولُهُ وَمَا زَادَهُمْ إِلَّا إِيمَنا وتسلما ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٢٢]. يَحْمِلُ هَذَا الدِّينَ مِنْ كُلِّ خَلَفٍ عُدُولُهُ، يَنْفُونَ عَنْهُ تَحْرِيفَ الْغَالِينَ، وَانْتِحَالَ الْجَاهِلِينَ، وَتَأْوِيلَ الْمُبْطِلِينَ. لَمْ يَمْتَحِنَّا بِمَا تَعْيَ الْعُقُولُ بِهِ حِرْصًا عَلَيْنَا فَلَمْ نَرْتَبْ وَلَمْ نَهِم. القسم الأول الدراسة
And Allah and His Messenger spoke the truth, and it only increased them in faith and submission. [Quran 33:22] 'Upright ones from every generation carry this religion, they remove from it the distortions of the extremists, the false claims of the ignorant, and the interpretations of the falsifiers.' He did not test us with what the intellects are incapable of, out of care for us, so we did not doubt nor waver. Section One: The Study.
Source pages p. 5

Commentary
This passage is the front matter of Bahr Ulum. It opens with a Quranic verse (33:22) praising believers who trust Allah and His Messenger. Then it includes a well-known hadith (often cited in Islamic scholarship) about the 'upright ones' (عُدُول) who preserve the religion from distortions, false attributions, and misinterpretations. This sets the tone for a work committed to orthodox understanding. A line from Imam al-Busiri's Burda follows, emphasizing that Allah has not burdened believers with intellectually impossible tests. Finally, the first section heading appears: 'The Study' (الدراسة), indicating the start of the main content. The passage serves as a pious introduction, grounding the logical study in religious authority and humility.

Key Terms
عُدُول
تَحْرِيف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) They are infallible prophets.
D) They memorize the entire Quran.

Key Takeaway
The front matter of Bahr Ulum uses Quran, hadith, and poetry to affirm divine authority and scholarly integrity before embarking on logical analysis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a Quranic verse or hadith in the opening of another Islamic text (e.g., al-Ash'ari's Maqalat al-Islamiyyin) and write a short paragraph explaining its rhetorical purpose.
?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Analyzing the Editor's Introduction to Sullam al-'Ulum
Editor opens with praise of Allah and Prophet, then introduces the book and author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze the structure and purpose of the editor's introduction to Sullam al-'Ulum and identify the key claims made about the book's significance and the author's independence.

Core Idea
The editor's praise frames the book as a product of independent Islamic thought, not a Greek imitation.

Every classical Islamic text typically begins with praise (hamdalah) and blessings (salawat), followed by a transition (wa ba'd) and an introduction. In this passage, the editor uses this structure to position Sullam al-'Ulum as a monumental work that exemplifies the independence and creativity of Islamic scholars. Understanding this framing is crucial for appreciating how this logic text fits into the broader Islamic intellectual tradition.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the hamdalah and salawat
Locate the praise of Allah and the blessings on the Prophet. Note the language of exaltation and submission, particularly the phrases 'سبحانك' and 'نشهد أن لا إله إلا أنت'.
This is a standard opening in Islamic scholarly works.
2
2. Note the transitional phrase 'wa ba'd'
After the religious invocations, the editor uses 'وبعد' (to proceed) to signal the start of the substantive introduction.
This phrase marks the shift from devotional to academic content.
3
3. Extract the key claims about the book
The editor calls Sullam al-'Ulum a 'magnificent book' in logic and claims it reveals the greatness of Islam, the purity of Islamic thought, and the independence of its scholars from foreign methodologies.
These claims set expectations about the book's originality and Islamic credentials.
4
4. Analyze the claim about the author
The author, Muhibb Allah al-Bahari al-Hindi, is described as a 'great investigator' and an imam. The editor emphasizes his lack of subservience to non-Islamic methodologies and his innovative thinking.
This highlights the tension between Islamic and Greek logical traditions.
5
5. Reflect on the purpose of such an introduction
Consider why the editor includes these claims: to legitimize the book within the Islamic tradition, to assert the value of independent Islamic scholarship, and to guide the reader's reception.
Such introductions are rhetorical: they shape how the text is understood and valued.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
افتتاحية المحقق

سبحانك، كيف لا يسبح بحمدك العقل الذي لا يجد في الوجود إلها سواك، وقد سجدت لعبقرية عظماء دينك جباه العلوم التي هي أعز ما يملكه من عاداك؟ ما أعظمك منعما، وما أضعفني شاكرا، وكيف لا يشكر نعمك القلب الذي لا يطمئن إلا بذكراك، وقد انخضعت لصولة أفكار الذاكرين لك أعناق الفنون التي ضلت نفوس المفتخرين بها عن أن تهواك؟ نشهد أن لا إله إلا أنت وحدك، لا شريك لك، وأن سيدنا محمدا عبدك ورسولك، ونصلي على هذا النبي الذي لو كان جميع الأنبياء أحياء في هذه الدنيا لما وسعهم إلا اتباعه، وهم جميعا في الدار الآخرة يأتون من بابه، ونسلم عليه وعليهم، وعلى آله وأصحابه، تسليما كثيرا نرجو به رحمة الله والنجاة من عقابه. وبعد،

فنحن اليوم مع كتاب جليل في علم المنطق، «سلم العلوم»، ومع صاحبه المحقق الكبير الشيخ الإمام محب الله البهاري الهندي رحمه الله، يتجلى في هذا الكتاب مظهر من مظاهر عظمة الإسلام، ومدى نصاعة الفكر الإسلامي الأصيل، ومبلغ استقلالية أئمته في التفكير والإبداع، وعدم تبعيتهم لأصحاب المناهج البعيدة عن هدي النبوة، وعدم جمودهم على ما تركه من
Editor's Introduction: Glory be to You, how could the intellect that finds no deity in existence other than You not glorify You with praise? And the foreheads of the sciences, which are the most precious possession of those who oppose You, have prostrated to the genius of the great ones of Your religion. How great You are as a benefactor, and how weak I am as a grateful one! And how could the heart that finds no tranquility except in Your remembrance not thank Your blessings? And the necks of the arts, whose souls of the proud have strayed from yearning for You, have bowed to the force of the thoughts of those who remember You. We bear witness that there is no god but You alone, with no partner, and that our master Muhammad is Your servant and Your Messenger. And we send blessings upon this Prophet such that if all the prophets were alive in this world, they would have no choice but to follow him, and they all in the hereafter come from his door. And we send peace upon him and upon them, and upon his family and companions, abundant peace by which we hope for Allah's mercy and salvation from His punishment. To proceed: Today we are with a magnificent book in the science of logic, 'Sullam al-'Ulum', and with its author, the great investigator, the Shaykh, the Imam, Muhibb Allah al-Bahari al-Hindi, may Allah have mercy on him. In this book, a manifestation of the greatness of Islam becomes evident, as well as the extent of the purity of authentic Islamic thought, the degree of independence of its imams in thinking and innovation, and their lack of subservience to the proponents of methodologies far from the guidance of prophethood, and their lack of stagnation on what was left by
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage is the editor's introduction. It begins with a lengthy praise of Allah and an invocation of blessings on the Prophet, emphasizing the Prophet's superiority over all other prophets. The phrase 'wa ba'd' (to proceed) is a standard transition in Arabic texts. The editor then introduces the book 'Sullam al-'Ulum' and its author, Muhibb Allah al-Bahari al-Hindi. The editor extols the book as a manifestation of Islamic greatness, highlighting the independence of Islamic scholars from foreign methodologies and their creative originality. The editor contrasts this with slavish adherence to non-Islamic thought. The introduction sets a reverent tone and establishes the book's significance within the Islamic intellectual tradition.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Understanding a Muhaqqiq's Introduction
Editor opens with praise of God and Prophet, then introduces the book and its author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key claims a muhaqqiq makes about a classical text's value and its relationship to Islamic intellectual tradition.

Core Idea
A muhaqqiq's introduction frames the text within the broader narrative of Islamic intellectual independence.

This passage is not part of the original matn but a modern editor's preface. It aims to situate 'Sullam al-Ulum' within the Islamic scholarly tradition, emphasizing its originality and its role in demonstrating the independence of Islamic thought from Greek civilization. By analyzing this introduction, you will learn how editors shape the reception of classical texts.

Guided Path
1
Locate the opening genre
Notice the opening formula: praise of God (tahmid) and blessings on the Prophet (tasliya). This is a standard feature of Islamic scholarly introductions, establishing the work within the Islamic tradition.
2
Identify the editor's main claims
The editor claims that the book 'Sullam al-Ulum' demonstrates the independence of Islamic thought from Greek civilization. Find the specific sentences that state this, such as 'the people of Islam were not a tail to Greek civilization'.
3
Assess the editor's evidence
The editor mentions that the book's theologians challenged others in their own arts. Is this evidence sufficient? Reflect on the difference between assertion and proof.
This step encourages critical reading of editorial framing.
4
Distinguish the editor from the author
The editor (muhaqqiq) is not the author. The passage is a modern introduction. Identify where the editor speaks about the author (al-Bahari) and where he expresses his own views.

فنحن اليوم مع كتاب جليل في علم المنطق، «سلم العلوم»، ومع صاحبه المحقق الكبير الشيخ الإمام محب الله البهاري الهندي رحمه الله ، يتجلى في هذا الكتاب مظهر من مظاهر عظمة الإسلام، ومدى نصاعة الفكر الإسلامي الأصيل، ومبلغ استقلالية أئمته في التفكير والإبداع، وعدم تبعيتهم لأصحاب المناهج البعيدة عن هدي النبوة، وعدم جمودهم على ما تركه من
غبر عبر الزمان ويُثبت الكتاب كيف أن أهل الإسلام لم يكن ذيلا لحضارة اليونان ، ولا ترديدا للثقافة الغربية، بل يثبت أن الإسلام كيف لفظ الفكر اليوناني لفظا قاسيا، ومجه مجا عنيفا.

كما أنه يصور تصويرا واضحا أن متكلمي أهل السنة كيف بارزوا رجال كل فن من تلك الفنون في فنونهم، وأفحموهم وغلبوهم. نعم، إنها حقيقة ساطعة تُرغِم أُنوفَ الحاسدين، وتقطع دابر شبهات الحاقدين، فعلى من يريد الوصول إلى الحق التزام طريق تؤديه إليه ؛ حتى لا تخطفه رياح الشبهات والأوهام، ولا تحول بينه وبين هدفه عقبات نصبها قطاع الطريق الأغوام.

فمما يُقرّب المسافة على باحث الحق، في مجال منهج التفكير والاستدلال، عند أجلة علماء الإسلام هذا الكتابُ الذي بين أيديكم الآن، وهو الكتاب الذي لا يدانيه كتاب في المنطق في أسلوب عرضه للمسائل. مع جزالة التعبير، ولطف المأخذ، وكثرة الفوائد، ولذة الابتكار. ومن هنا كثرت عليه الشروح والحواشي والتعليقات، كثرةً لم أجد لها نظيرا لأي كتاب هذا الفن، في طول تاريخه، وطبع كثير منها طبعات عدة. وكنا نقرأه بعض شروحه في حلقات الدروس المسجدية في مليبار»، بعد قرائتنا لـ«شرح الشمسية» للقطب الرازي رَحِمَهُ الله ، إلا أنها لم تكن على مستوى قرائة من سبقنا من المشايخ، حيث تَدَهْوَرَ النشاط العلمي وطُوي بساطه من تحت الأقدام، على الرغم من اتساع حال المعيشة وتوفر أدوات التحصيل.

ومن عجب أن أمر هذا الكتاب لم يشغل أذهان العلماء في البلاد العربية، بل منهم من لم يسمع عن هذا الكتاب شيئا، وهم الأكثر، وعندما أتيحت لي جلسات علمية مع بعض فضلاء مصر من شباب هذا الجيل
Glory be to You! How can the intellect that finds no deity other than You in existence not glorify You with praise? Indeed, the foreheads of the sciences—which are the dearest possession of those who oppose You—have prostrated before the genius of the great ones of Your religion. How great You are as a Benefactor, and how weak I am as a thankful one! And how can the heart that finds no tranquility except in Your remembrance not thank Your blessings? Indeed, the necks of the arts—whose boastful souls have strayed from loving You—have bowed to the overwhelming power of the thoughts of those who remember You. We bear witness that there is no god but You alone, without partner, and that our master Muhammad is Your servant and messenger. And we send blessings upon this Prophet—if all the prophets were alive in this world, nothing would suffice them except following him, and they all in the Hereafter will come through his door—and we send peace upon him and upon them, and upon his family and companions, abundant peace by which we hope for the mercy of Allah and salvation from His punishment. Afterward...

Today we are with a great book in the science of logic, 'Sullam al-Ulum,' and with its author, the great investigator, the Imam, the beloved of Allah, al-Bahari al-Hindi—may Allah have mercy on him. In this book shines a manifestation of the greatness of Islam, the brilliance of authentic Islamic thought, the extent of the independence of its imams in thinking and creativity, and their lack of subservience to the proponents of methodologies far from prophetic guidance, and their lack of stagnation on what was left by those who passed through time. The book demonstrates how the people of Islam were not a tail to Greek civilization nor a repetition of Western culture; rather, it proves how Islam vigorously rejected Greek thought and violently expelled it.

Likewise, it vividly depicts how the theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah challenged the men of each of those arts in their own arts, and silenced them and overcame them. Yes, it is a glaring truth that forces the noses of the envious to rub in the dust and cuts off the root of the doubts of the spiteful. So whoever wants to reach the truth must adhere to a path that leads to it, so that the winds of doubts and illusions do not snatch him away, nor the obstacles set up by highwaymen block him from his goal.

Among the things that shorten the distance for the seeker of truth, in the field of methodology of thinking and reasoning, according to the venerable scholars of Islam, is this book now in your hands. It is a book unmatched by any other book on logic in its style of presenting issues, with its forceful expression, gentle approach, abundant benefits, and delightful innovation. Hence, numerous commentaries, glosses, and notes have been written on it—a multitude I have not seen paralleled for any book in this art throughout its entire history. Many of them have been published in several editions. We used to read some of its commentaries in the mosque study circles in Malabar, after our reading of 'Sharh al-Shamsiyya' by al-Qutb al-Razi—may Allah have mercy on him—but they were not at the level of the recitation of our predecessors among the shaykhs, as scientific activity had declined and its carpet was rolled up from under the feet, despite the expansion of living conditions and the availability of tools for learning.

It is a wonder that this book has not occupied the minds of scholars in the Arab lands; rather, most of them have not even heard of this book. When I had scientific sessions with some of the virtuous youth of Egypt from this generation...
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage is the muhaqqiq's (investigator's) introduction to the book 'Bahr Ulum' (a commentary on 'Sullam al-Ulum'). It opens with a lengthy praise of Allah and blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad, emphasizing the uniqueness of Allah and the necessity of following the Prophet. The editor then introduces the book 'Sullam al-Ulum' and its author, al-Bahari al-Hindi, highlighting the book's significance in the field of logic. He argues that this book demonstrates the independence and originality of Islamic thought, showing that Muslims did not simply imitate Greek or Western culture but critically engaged with it. He also notes that the theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah refuted the proponents of other disciplines. The editor praises the book's style and content, noting its many commentaries, and expresses surprise that it is not well-known in the Arab world. The passage serves as an enthusiastic endorsement of the work and sets the stage for the commentary that follows.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Editor's Introduction: The Distinctiveness of Islamic Logic
Editor's argument for Islamic logic's independence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and analyze the editor's argument that Islamic logic is independent and distinct from Greek philosophy, using evidence from his introduction.

Core Idea
Islamic logic is not a copy of Greek thought, but an independent tradition that critically engaged and overcame it.

The editor of Bahr al-Ulum's commentary on Sullam al-Ulum opens with a bold assertion: Islamic thought is not a derivative of Greek civilization but a unique intellectual tradition that confronted and surpassed it. This lesson helps you unpack that claim and understand its implications for the study of logic in the Islamic world. You will learn how to trace the editor's argumentative moves and evaluate his evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's central thesis
Find the sentence where the editor states his main claim about Islam and Greek thought. The passage asserts that Islam 'expelled Greek thought harshly and rejected it violently.'
Look for the contrast between 'tail to Greek civilization' and the independent nature of Islamic scholars.
2
Examine the evidence he provides
List the examples he gives: theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah confronting and overcoming other scholars, and the unique style of Sullam al-Ulum that no other logic book matches.
Consider how these examples support the claim of independence.
3
Analyze the rhetorical tone
Note the emotive language ('glaring fact', 'expelled harshly', 'cut off the traces of doubts'). How does this reinforce the argument?
The tone is confident and confrontational, aiming to persuade the reader.
4
Contextualize the book's significance
According to the editor, why is Sullam al-Ulum an important text? He mentions its rich expression, subtle approach, abundance of benefits, and innovation.
This establishes the book as a key response to Greek influences.

شرح بحر العلوم على سلم العلوم
غبر عبر الزمان ويُثبت الكتاب كيف أن أهل الإسلام لم يكن ذيلا لحضارة اليونان ، ولا ترديدا للثقافة الغربية، بل يثبت أن الإسلام كيف لفظ الفكر اليوناني لفظا قاسيا، ومجه مجا عنيفا.
كما أنه يصور تصويرا واضحا أن متكلمي أهل السنة كيف بارزوا رجال كل فن من تلك الفنون في فنونهم، وأفحموهم وغلبوهم. نعم، إنها حقيقة ساطعة تُرغِم أُنوفَ الحاسدين، وتقطع دابر شبهات الحاقدين، فعلى من يريد الوصول إلى الحق التزام طريق تؤديه إليه ؛ حتى لا تخطفه رياح الشبهات والأوهام، ولا تحول بينه وبين هدفه عقبات نصبها قطاع الطريق الأغوام.
فمما يُقرّب المسافة على باحث الحق، في مجال منهج التفكير والاستدلال، عند أجلة علماء الإسلام هذا الكتابُ الذي بين أيديكم الآن، وهو الكتاب الذي لا يدانيه كتاب في المنطق في أسلوب عرضه للمسائل. مع جزالة التعبير، ولطف المأخذ، وكثرة الفوائد، ولذة الابتكار. ومن هنا كثرت عليه الشروح والحواشي والتعليقات، كثرةً لم أجد لها نظيرا لأي كتاب هذا الفن، في طول تاريخه، وطبع كثير منها طبعات عدة. وكنا نقرأه بعض شروحه في حلقات الدروس المسجدية في مليبار»، بعد قرائتنا لـ«شرح الشمسية» للقطب الرازي رَحِمَهُ الله ، إلا أنها لم تكن على مستوى قرائة من سبقنا من المشايخ، حيث تَدَهْوَرَ النشاط العلمي وطُوي بساطه من تحت الأقدام، على الرغم من اتساع حال المعيشة وتوفر أدوات التحصيل.
ومن عجب أن أمر هذا الكتاب لم يشغل أذهان العلماء في البلاد العربية، بل منهم من لم يسمع عن هذا الكتاب شيئا، وهم الأكثر، وعندما أتيحت لي جلسات علمية مع بعض فضلاء مصر من شباب هذا الجيل افتتاحية المحقق اكور وجدوني فوائده، فوجدتهم يحرقهم الشوق إليه وإلى قرائته واقتناء نفائسه. وكنتُ قد عزمت قبلا على خدمته وتقريبه إلى عشاق العلم في العالم العربي، وبدأت في جمع أهم شروحه، وإعادة صفها وشرح غموضها وبيان مشكلها؛ رجاء خدمة هذا الدين الحنيف، ورَوْمَ تخليد ذكر أئمته الفضلاء، والكل لابتغاء مرضاة رب العالمين.
و قسمت هذا العمل إلى قسمين رئيسيين: قسم الدراسة، وقسم التحقيق يشتمل القسم الأول على الدراسة المتعلقة بالعلوم العقلية التي يعتبر المنطق جزء مهما منها، وبالهند وحالة العلوم العقلية فيها، وبشخصية المصنف والشارح، وكلمة عن الكتاب وشرحه، وقسمت هذا القسم إلى الأبواب، وهي إلى الفصول، والفصول إلى المباحث. وهذه الدراسة مما لم يكن منها بد؛ حيث لا يتم الغرض المطلوب من إخراج هذا الكتاب إلا به. وأما القسم الثاني فهو محط الرحل؛ حيث هو عبارة عن نص الكتاب مع الشرح.
فهذا هو «سلم العلوم ، أزفه إلى أهل العلم في حلة قشيبة، مع شرح العلامة الإمام عبد العلي بحر العلوم رَحمَهُ اللهُ ، سوف يستفيد العالم والطالب منه الكثير إن شاء الله ، وهذا هو المنطق الذي أكد على شرف الحيوانية بشرط انضمام الناطقية، وهذا هو الإسلام الذي لم تطمس الشيخوخة شيئا، ولا أفقدته القدرة على اقتحام العقبات يتجلى ذلك كله في هذا العمل الذي نضيفه اليوم إلى نظائره السابقة من عندنا أو من غيرنا، وسيتلوه ما يصدقه ويدعمه حتى تقوم الساعة .
ولا يفوتني كلمة الشكر لأهله، وهم كثر، منهم ذوو النفوس المترفعة
Explanation of Bahr al-Ulum on Sullam al-Ulum. It passes across time and the book proves how the people of Islam were not a tail to Greek civilization, nor a repetition of Western culture, but rather proves how Islam expelled Greek thought harshly and rejected it violently. Likewise, it clearly depicts how the theologians of the Ahl al-Sunnah confronted the men of every art in their arts, and silenced them and overcame them. Yes, it is a glaring fact that forces the noses of the envious and cuts off the traces of the doubts of the haters. So upon whoever desires to reach the truth is to follow a path that leads him to it, so that the winds of doubts and illusions do not snatch him away, and the obstacles set up by the highwaymen of the ignorant do not come between him and his goal. Among what brings near the distance for the seeker of truth, in the field of the method of thinking and inference, according to the eminent scholars of Islam, is this book that is now in your hands. It is a book that no other book in logic rivals in its style of presenting issues, with richness of expression, subtlety of approach, abundance of benefits, and pleasure of innovation. Hence, many commentaries, glosses, and annotations have been written on it, a multitude I have not found equal for any book of this art, in its entire history, and many of them have been printed several times. We used to read some of its commentaries in mosque study circles in Malabar, after reading 'Sharh al-Shamsiyya' by al-Qutb al-Razi (may God have mercy on him), but they were not at the level of the reading of our predecessors among the scholars, as scientific activity declined and its carpet was folded from under the feet, despite the expansion of living conditions and the availability of tools of acquisition. And it is surprising that the matter of this book did not occupy the minds of scholars in the Arab countries; rather, some of them have not heard anything about this book, and they are the majority. When I had scientific sessions with some virtuous people of Egypt from the youth of this generation... the editor's opening [word]... I found that they burned with longing for it, for reading it and acquiring its gems. I had previously resolved to serve it and bring it closer to the lovers of knowledge in the Arab world, and I began to collect its most important commentaries, rearrange them, explain their obscurities, and clarify their difficulties, hoping to serve this true religion and aiming to immortalize the memory of its virtuous imams, and all for seeking the pleasure of the Lord of the Worlds. I divided this work into two main sections: a study section and an editing section. The first section includes the study concerning the rational sciences, of which logic is an important part, and about India and the state of the rational sciences therein, and about the personality of the author and the commentator, and a word about the book and its commentary. I divided this section into chapters, chapters into sections, and sections into investigations. This study was indispensable, as the desired purpose of producing this book cannot be achieved without it. As for the second section, it is the main focus, as it consists of the text of the book with the commentary. This is 'Sullam al-Ulum', which I present to the people of knowledge in a new garb, with the commentary of the distinguished scholar Imam Abd al-Ali Bahr al-Ulum (may God have mercy on him). The scholar and the student will benefit greatly from it, God willing. This is the logic that emphasized the honor of animality on condition of the inclusion of rationality, and this is Islam which old age has not obliterated anything, nor has it lost its ability to overcome obstacles. All that is manifested in this work which we add today to its previous counterparts from us or from others, and what confirms and supports it will follow until the Hour is established. And I do not neglect a word of thanks to its people, who are many, among them those with elevated souls.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is the editor's (muhaqqiq) preface or introduction to the edition of Bahr al-Ulum's commentary on Sullam al-Ulum. The editor begins by asserting the distinctiveness of Islamic thought, contrasting it with Greek civilization and Western culture. He claims that Islam did not merely follow or repeat Greek philosophy but actively rejected it. He then praises the theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah for confronting and overcoming scholars of other disciplines. The editor emphasizes that Sullam al-Ulum is an exceptional book in logic, unmatched in its style, eloquence, and innovative approach, which attracted many commentaries and glosses. He shares his personal experience of studying it in Malabar and notes the decline of scholarly activity despite material prosperity. The editor expresses surprise that the book is not well-known in Arab countries, even among the youth of Egypt. He states his intention to serve the book by collecting its important commentaries, clarifying difficulties, and publishing it in two parts: a study section covering the rational sciences, India, and the author/commentator, and an edition section containing the text and commentary. He concludes by presenting this work as a contribution to Islamic thought and expressing gratitude to those who assisted.

Key Takeaway

Introduction and Front Matter

Editorial Methodology: How to Serve a Classic Text
Editor's methodology for critical edition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to outline the editor's methodology for producing a critical edition of a classical Islamic text, as described in his introduction.

Core Idea
A scholarly edition of a classical text requires both contextual study and careful text collation.

The editor of Bahr al-Ulum's commentary does not simply reprint the text; he provides a comprehensive two-part work: a study of the rational sciences, the Indian context, and the authors, followed by the edited text. This lesson helps you understand his methodology and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main sections of the work
Find where the editor describes the division. He says: 'I divided this work into two main sections: a study section and an editing section.'
Note the Arabic terms: قسم الدراسة (study section) and قسم التحقيق (edition section).
2
List the contents of the first section (study)
The editor mentions: the rational sciences (including logic), India and its rational sciences, the personality of the author and commentator, and a word about the book and its commentary.
This section provides essential background for understanding the text.
3
Note his reason for including the study
He states that the study is 'indispensable' and 'the desired purpose cannot be achieved without it.'
This emphasizes the importance of context in textual scholarship.
4
Describe the second section's focus
The second section contains the text of the book (matn) along with the commentary (sharh).
This is the core of the edition.
5
Evaluate his approach
Consider how this methodology serves the reader: the study provides the necessary background to appreciate the text, while the edited text ensures accuracy.
This is a model for critical editions in Islamic studies.

شرح بحر العلوم على سلم العلوم
غبر عبر الزمان ويُثبت الكتاب كيف أن أهل الإسلام لم يكن ذيلا لحضارة اليونان ، ولا ترديدا للثقافة الغربية، بل يثبت أن الإسلام كيف لفظ الفكر اليوناني لفظا قاسيا، ومجه مجا عنيفا.
كما أنه يصور تصويرا واضحا أن متكلمي أهل السنة كيف بارزوا رجال كل فن من تلك الفنون في فنونهم، وأفحموهم وغلبوهم. نعم، إنها حقيقة ساطعة تُرغِم أُنوفَ الحاسدين، وتقطع دابر شبهات الحاقدين، فعلى من يريد الوصول إلى الحق التزام طريق تؤديه إليه ؛ حتى لا تخطفه رياح الشبهات والأوهام، ولا تحول بينه وبين هدفه عقبات نصبها قطاع الطريق الأغوام.
فمما يُقرّب المسافة على باحث الحق، في مجال منهج التفكير والاستدلال، عند أجلة علماء الإسلام هذا الكتابُ الذي بين أيديكم الآن، وهو الكتاب الذي لا يدانيه كتاب في المنطق في أسلوب عرضه للمسائل. مع جزالة التعبير، ولطف المأخذ، وكثرة الفوائد، ولذة الابتكار. ومن هنا كثرت عليه الشروح والحواشي والتعليقات، كثرةً لم أجد لها نظيرا لأي كتاب هذا الفن، في طول تاريخه، وطبع كثير منها طبعات عدة. وكنا نقرأه بعض شروحه في حلقات الدروس المسجدية في مليبار»، بعد قرائتنا لـ«شرح الشمسية» للقطب الرازي رَحِمَهُ الله ، إلا أنها لم تكن على مستوى قرائة من سبقنا من المشايخ، حيث تَدَهْوَرَ النشاط العلمي وطُوي بساطه من تحت الأقدام، على الرغم من اتساع حال المعيشة وتوفر أدوات التحصيل.
ومن عجب أن أمر هذا الكتاب لم يشغل أذهان العلماء في البلاد العربية، بل منهم من لم يسمع عن هذا الكتاب شيئا، وهم الأكثر، وعندما أتيحت لي جلسات علمية مع بعض فضلاء مصر من شباب هذا الجيل افتتاحية المحقق اكور وجدوني فوائده، فوجدتهم يحرقهم الشوق إليه وإلى قرائته واقتناء نفائسه. وكنتُ قد عزمت قبلا على خدمته وتقريبه إلى عشاق العلم في العالم العربي، وبدأت في جمع أهم شروحه، وإعادة صفها وشرح غموضها وبيان مشكلها؛ رجاء خدمة هذا الدين الحنيف، ورَوْمَ تخليد ذكر أئمته الفضلاء، والكل لابتغاء مرضاة رب العالمين.
و قسمت هذا العمل إلى قسمين رئيسيين: قسم الدراسة، وقسم التحقيق يشتمل القسم الأول على الدراسة المتعلقة بالعلوم العقلية التي يعتبر المنطق جزء مهما منها، وبالهند وحالة العلوم العقلية فيها، وبشخصية المصنف والشارح، وكلمة عن الكتاب وشرحه، وقسمت هذا القسم إلى الأبواب، وهي إلى الفصول، والفصول إلى المباحث. وهذه الدراسة مما لم يكن منها بد؛ حيث لا يتم الغرض المطلوب من إخراج هذا الكتاب إلا به. وأما القسم الثاني فهو محط الرحل؛ حيث هو عبارة عن نص الكتاب مع الشرح.
فهذا هو «سلم العلوم ، أزفه إلى أهل العلم في حلة قشيبة، مع شرح العلامة الإمام عبد العلي بحر العلوم رَحمَهُ اللهُ ، سوف يستفيد العالم والطالب منه الكثير إن شاء الله ، وهذا هو المنطق الذي أكد على شرف الحيوانية بشرط انضمام الناطقية، وهذا هو الإسلام الذي لم تطمس الشيخوخة شيئا، ولا أفقدته القدرة على اقتحام العقبات يتجلى ذلك كله في هذا العمل الذي نضيفه اليوم إلى نظائره السابقة من عندنا أو من غيرنا، وسيتلوه ما يصدقه ويدعمه حتى تقوم الساعة .
ولا يفوتني كلمة الشكر لأهله، وهم كثر، منهم ذوو النفوس المترفعة
Explanation of Bahr al-Ulum on Sullam al-Ulum. It passes across time and the book proves how the people of Islam were not a tail to Greek civilization, nor a repetition of Western culture, but rather proves how Islam expelled Greek thought harshly and rejected it violently. Likewise, it clearly depicts how the theologians of the Ahl al-Sunnah confronted the men of every art in their arts, and silenced them and overcame them. Yes, it is a glaring fact that forces the noses of the envious and cuts off the traces of the doubts of the haters. So upon whoever desires to reach the truth is to follow a path that leads him to it, so that the winds of doubts and illusions do not snatch him away, and the obstacles set up by the highwaymen of the ignorant do not come between him and his goal. Among what brings near the distance for the seeker of truth, in the field of the method of thinking and inference, according to the eminent scholars of Islam, is this book that is now in your hands. It is a book that no other book in logic rivals in its style of presenting issues, with richness of expression, subtlety of approach, abundance of benefits, and pleasure of innovation. Hence, many commentaries, glosses, and annotations have been written on it, a multitude I have not found equal for any book of this art, in its entire history, and many of them have been printed several times. We used to read some of its commentaries in mosque study circles in Malabar, after reading 'Sharh al-Shamsiyya' by al-Qutb al-Razi (may God have mercy on him), but they were not at the level of the reading of our predecessors among the scholars, as scientific activity declined and its carpet was folded from under the feet, despite the expansion of living conditions and the availability of tools of acquisition. And it is surprising that the matter of this book did not occupy the minds of scholars in the Arab countries; rather, some of them have not heard anything about this book, and they are the majority. When I had scientific sessions with some virtuous people of Egypt from the youth of this generation... the editor's opening [word]... I found that they burned with longing for it, for reading it and acquiring its gems. I had previously resolved to serve it and bring it closer to the lovers of knowledge in the Arab world, and I began to collect its most important commentaries, rearrange them, explain their obscurities, and clarify their difficulties, hoping to serve this true religion and aiming to immortalize the memory of its virtuous imams, and all for seeking the pleasure of the Lord of the Worlds. I divided this work into two main sections: a study section and an editing section. The first section includes the study concerning the rational sciences, of which logic is an important part, and about India and the state of the rational sciences therein, and about the personality of the author and the commentator, and a word about the book and its commentary. I divided this section into chapters, chapters into sections, and sections into investigations. This study was indispensable, as the desired purpose of producing this book cannot be achieved without it. As for the second section, it is the main focus, as it consists of the text of the book with the commentary. This is 'Sullam al-Ulum', which I present to the people of knowledge in a new garb, with the commentary of the distinguished scholar Imam Abd al-Ali Bahr al-Ulum (may God have mercy on him). The scholar and the student will benefit greatly from it, God willing. This is the logic that emphasized the honor of animality on condition of the inclusion of rationality, and this is Islam which old age has not obliterated anything, nor has it lost its ability to overcome obstacles. All that is manifested in this work which we add today to its previous counterparts from us or from others, and what confirms and supports it will follow until the Hour is established. And I do not neglect a word of thanks to its people, who are many, among them those with elevated souls.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This passage is the editor's (muhaqqiq) preface or introduction to the edition of Bahr al-Ulum's commentary on Sullam al-Ulum. The editor begins by asserting the distinctiveness of Islamic thought, contrasting it with Greek civilization and Western culture. He claims that Islam did not merely follow or repeat Greek philosophy but actively rejected it. He then praises the theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah for confronting and overcoming scholars of other disciplines. The editor emphasizes that Sullam al-Ulum is an exceptional book in logic, unmatched in its style, eloquence, and innovative approach, which attracted many commentaries and glosses. He shares his personal experience of studying it in Malabar and notes the decline of scholarly activity despite material prosperity. The editor expresses surprise that the book is not well-known in Arab countries, even among the youth of Egypt. He states his intention to serve the book by collecting its important commentaries, clarifying difficulties, and publishing it in two parts: a study section covering the rational sciences, India, and the author/commentator, and an edition section containing the text and commentary. He concludes by presenting this work as a contribution to Islamic thought and expressing gratitude to those who assisted.

Introduction and Front Matter

Navigating a Scholarly Preface in Islamic Logic Editions
Editor introduces his edition, motivation, and structure of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract the structure, motivation, and scope of an academic edition from its preface.

Core Idea
A scholarly preface is a roadmap to the edition's purpose, structure, and context.

When you pick up an edition of a classical text like Sullam al-Ulum, the editor's preface might seem like mere formalities. In reality, it contains vital information: why the book was reissued, how it is organized, and what intellectual background is relevant. This lesson teaches you how to mine such a preface for key data that will orient your reading of the entire work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editor's motivation
Look for phrases indicating why the editor undertook the edition. In this preface, the editor notes that scholars 'burn with longing' for the book, and he wants to 'serve the upright religion' and 'immortalize the memory of its virtuous imams.' This tells you the edition is meant to revive a significant text.
2
Locate the work's main components
The editor explicitly states the work has two sections: a 'study section' (qism al-dirasa) and a 'verification section' (qism al-tahqiq). The study section covers intellectual sciences, India's context, author and commentator biographies; the verification section contains the actual text and commentary.
Recognizing this structure helps you find the original matn quickly.
3
Note the editorial process described
The editor mentions collecting important commentaries, reordering them, explaining obscurities, and clarifying difficulties. This indicates a critical edition with explanatory work.
Such details are crucial for evaluating the edition's reliability.
4
Understand the intellectual context highlighted
The preface places logic within the 'intellectual sciences' (al-ulum al-aqliyya) and mentions India's role. This orients the reader to the tradition from which the text emerged.
Even brief mentions of context can be valuable for historical understanding.

Editor's Preface: I repeated and found its benefits, and I found them burning with longing for it and for reading it and acquiring its rarities. I had mentioned this book with veneration and exaltation, and pointed to its merits and some. I previously resolved to serve it and bring it closer to lovers of knowledge in the Arab world, and I began collecting its most important commentaries, reordering them, explaining their obscurities and clarifying their difficulties; hoping to serve this upright religion, and aiming to immortalize the memory of its virtuous imams, all seeking the pleasure of the Lord of the Worlds. I divided this work into two main sections: a study section and a verification section. The first section includes the study related to the intellectual sciences, of which logic is an important part, and regarding India and the state of the intellectual sciences there, and concerning the personality of the author and commentator, and a word about the book and its commentary. I divided this section into parts, which are divided into chapters, and chapters into topics. This study was indispensable; for the desired purpose of producing this book cannot be achieved without it. As for the second section, it is the main subject; it consists of the text of the book with the commentary. So this is 'Sullam al-Ulum', I present it to the people of knowledge in a new garb, with the commentary of the distinguished Imam Abdul Ali Bahr al-Ulum, may God have mercy on him. The scholar and student will benefit from it greatly, God willing. This is the logic that affirmed the honor of animality on condition of rationality, and this is Islam that old age has not erased anything, nor lost its ability to surmount obstacles. All of this is reflected in this work that we add today to previous similar works from us or others, and it will be followed by what confirms and supports it until the Hour. From his genius. I cannot miss a word of thanks to its people, and they are many, among them those with lofty souls from above Sharh Bahr al-Ulum 'ala Sullam al-Ulum that their names be mentioned or their efforts thanked. Their concern was only to seek the pleasure of the Generous One, whose essence is impossible to conceive. So O God, take their hands—and our hands with them—to You as the generous are taken. I ask the Lord for success and facilitation to continue serving 'Sullam al-Ulum' in teaching and publication, as well as serving its other important commentaries—at least the commentaries of Mulla Hasan, Qadi Mubarak, and Hamd Allah—in the near future. Indeed, He does not disappoint those who hope in Him, nor does He reject those who call on Him. Our last call is that praise be to God, Lord of the Worlds, and blessings be upon our master Muhammad and his family and all his Companions. Abd al-Nasir Ahmad al-Malibari al-Shafi'i, Cairo, Egypt, Jumada al-Thani 26, 1433 AH, May 17, 2012 CE.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage is the editor's preface to the edition of 'Sullam al-Ulum' with the commentary of Bahr al-Ulum. The editor describes his motivation: after noticing the high demand and appreciation for the book, he decided to serve it by collecting its important commentaries, clarifying obscurities, and producing a structured edition. He divides his work into two main sections: (1) a study section that covers intellectual sciences, logic, the context of India, the biography of the author and commentator, and an overview of the book; and (2) a verification section containing the text with the commentary. He emphasizes that the study section is essential for achieving the purpose of the edition. He then praises the logic text, calling it a work that affirms the honor of animality with rationality, and expresses hope that it will benefit scholars and students. He thanks those who contributed and prays for success in his future publications.

Introduction and Front Matter

Structure of the Preliminary Study Section
Author lists the three chapters of the introductory study section.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the three chapters of the preliminary study section and explain their purpose.

Core Idea
A book's preface reveals the author's scholarly context and aims.

This passage is the table of contents for the first section of Bahr al-Ulum's commentary. It lists three chapters that set the stage for the logical work to come. Understanding this structure helps you situate the text within its historical and intellectual context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the section title and function
The Arabic begins with 'القسم الأول الدراسة حول الكتاب' which translates to 'The first section: Study about the book.' This tells you that this entire section is a preliminary study, not the main commentary.
Preliminary sections often provide background and context.
2
List the three chapters as numbered
The passage explicitly lists three chapters: (1) الهند والعلوم العقلية (India and rational sciences), (2) لمحة موجزة عن المصنف (A brief glimpse of the author), (3) نبذة يسرة عن الشارح (A little information about the commentator).
The numbers indicate clear separation of topics.
3
Infer the purpose of each chapter from its title
From the titles, chapter 1 likely discusses the historical background of rational sciences in India. Chapter 2 provides a biography of the author (possibly al-Akhdari). Chapter 3 introduces the commentator (Bahr al-Ulum himself).
This helps you anticipate what information to expect in each chapter.
4
Recognize that this is not the commentary proper
The phrase 'الدراسة حول الكتاب' indicates this is a study about the book, not the commentary on the matn. The actual commentary likely starts in a later section.
Avoid the common misunderstanding of treating this as the beginning of the main content.

Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents outlining the first major section of the work, which is a study about the book itself. Contextualizing Rational Sciences in India: Author's Introduction
Author introduces India's intellectual history and necessity of discussing rational sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's motivation for discussing India's rational heritage and explain why understanding this historical context is essential for studying Islamic logic.

Core Idea
India's ancient polytheism shaped its rational sciences, but Islam transformed it into a fertile ground for Islamic thought.

The author opens his commentary by describing India's dual character: a land deeply rooted in polytheism and mythology, yet also a place where Islam flourished and produced a rich rational heritage. This introduction is not about logic itself, but it sets the stage for why the rational sciences — including logic — must be understood in their historical and civilizational context. As you read, pay attention to how the author contrasts the ancient Indian traditions with the later Islamic scholarly activity, and note his concern about foreign ideas entering Islamic curricula.

This shows the transformation.

This is the motivation for the book.

الهند ، كما هو معروف لدى الكثير من الناس، بلاد الأسرار والأساطير، مجمع شعوب وطبقات، تكثر فيها الأديان والثقافات، وتتعدد اللغات والعادات، وهي تعتبر واحدة من بقاع العالم التي استوطنها البشر منذ أقدم العصور، قد اعترف لها بالحكمة، وأقرَّ لها بالتبرز في فنون المعارف، ولعظمائهم السِّيَر الفاضلة ، والملكات المحمودة، والسياسات الكاملة. كما يعرف المطلع على التاريخ القديم ـ من أعرق بلاد وهي في الوثنية، فهي فيها قديمة وأصيلة ؛ إذ كانت في كثير من البلاد وافدة جديدة، وفكرةً دخيلة، وقد عجنت فلسفتها وحضارتها وآدابها، وعلومها المتعلقة بالفلك والرياضة والتقويم، فضلا عن الديانات ، بهذه الوثنية الماجنة، وما نشأ عنها من الأوهام والخيالات، فهي أرض المؤلهين والمؤلهات، وأرض الأساطير والروايات وأرض الأعياد والمواسم، والمهرجانات والمآتم ؛ تذكارا لحوادث تاريخية دينية ، وأبطال قومية خرافية . والهند بعد ذلك كله أو قبله من أخصب بلاد الله تعالى للإسلام، حيث احتضنته ومكنته من النماء والانتشار، من جنوبها إلى شمالها، ومن غربها إلى شرقها . أينما توجهت في الهند، مُشَرِّقًا أو مُغَرِّباً ، مقبلا أو مدبرا، فلن تستطيع أن تهرب من منظر إسلامي جميل، في مساجدها الفخمة، ومدارسها المعمورة، وجامعاتها الشامخة، وحتى في مظاهر الحياة الفردية والاجتماعية، بشكل واضح، يعرف ذلك من تعرف على المجتمع الهندي المسلم بلا شك. فالحديث عن الهند ذو شجون، نورد منه ما تمس إليه حاجتنا حين تقديم هذا الكتاب إلى جماهير القراء والمثقفين؛ للاطلاع على طرف مما يتعلق بالحالة الحضارية والفكرية والدينية فيها . كما أن النشاط العلمي في المجتمعات الإسلامية يحتاج إلى تحليل وتفصيل؛ حيث إنه قد حدث فيه التوسع والتطور، وانضاف إليه في الأزمنة المتأخرة ما كان غريبا عن روح الإسلام من فروع العلم، وانضم إليه من الفنون والمعارف ما لم يكن يمارسه إلا أهلُ ملةٍ أو نحلة أو فرقة أو بدعة، مخالفة لمنهج أهل الإسلام، ومذهب أهل السنة. حتى وصل الأمر إلى حد أن صارت لدينا كمية هائلة من التراث العقلي، تركها رجال أهل السنة المتكلمين والمناطقة والمفكرين، ودخلت في مناهج الدراسة في حلقات الدروس المسجدية وقاعات الجامعات العالمية، من مشارق البلاد الإسلامية إلى مغاربها فلا بد من الحديث عن هذا الموضوع والإشارة الموجزة إلى حل بعض الإشكالية المعقدة التي نشأت عن هذا التطور. وهذا هو التمهيد المجمل لباب الهند والعلوم العقلية ، نتناول جزئياته خلال الفصول والمباحث التالية:
India, as is known to many people, is a land of secrets and myths, a gathering of peoples and classes, abundant in religions and cultures, and diverse in languages and customs. It is considered one of the regions of the world inhabited by humans since ancient times. It has been acknowledged for wisdom and affirmed for excellence in the arts of knowledge, and its great men have virtuous biographies, praiseworthy qualities, and complete policies. Likewise, one who is acquainted with ancient history knows that it is one of the most ancient lands in polytheism; it is ancient and original in it, whereas in many other lands it was a new arrival and an alien idea. Its philosophy, civilization, literature, and sciences related to astronomy, mathematics, and the calendar, besides religions, were kneaded with this impure polytheism and what arose from it of illusions and fantasies. It is the land of deified males and females, the land of myths and stories, the land of festivals and seasons, festivals and mournings, as commemorations of religious historical events and legendary national heroes. After all that or before it, India is among the most fertile lands of Allah Almighty for Islam, for it embraced it and enabled it to grow and spread, from its south to its north, from its west to its east. Wherever you go in India, eastward or westward, coming or going, you cannot escape a beautiful Islamic scene, in its magnificent mosques, its flourishing schools, its towering universities, and even in the manifestations of individual and social life, clearly. Whoever becomes acquainted with the Indian Muslim community knows that without a doubt. So talking about India has many branches; we mention from it what we need when presenting this book to the masses of readers and intellectuals, to get a glimpse of what relates to the civilizational, intellectual, and religious situation therein. Also, scientific activity in Islamic societies needs analysis and detail; for there has occurred in it expansion and development, and in later times there was added to it what was foreign to the spirit of Islam from branches of science, and there joined it from arts and sciences that only people of a certain religion, sect, faction, or innovation used to practice, contrary to the methodology of the people of Islam and the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunnah. Until it reached a point where we have a huge amount of rational heritage, left by the men of Ahl al-Sunnah, the theologians, logicians, and thinkers, and it entered into the curricula of study in mosque study circles and halls of global universities, from the eastern lands of Islam to its western lands. So it is necessary to talk about this subject and briefly indicate solving some of the complex problem that arose from this development. This is the brief introduction to the chapter on India and the rational sciences, which we will discuss in detail in the following chapters and sections.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is an introductory section from the author of *Bahr Ulum*, setting the context for his commentary on logic and rational sciences. He begins by describing India's ancient and diverse heritage, noting its deep roots in polytheism and the resulting myths and philosophies. Despite this, he emphasizes that India became fertile ground for Islam, with a visible Islamic presence in architecture, education, and daily life. The author then shifts to discuss the development of scientific activity in Islamic societies, noting that over time, foreign elements have entered the sciences, including branches that were once exclusive to other religions or sects. This has led to a large body of rational heritage that is now studied worldwide. The author states that his book aims to address the complexities arising from this development, specifically focusing on the rational sciences in India. This is a front_matter passage that lays the groundwork for the subsequent chapters.

Key Terms
التراث العقلي (al-turāth al-ʿaqlī): The rational heritage left by Ahl al-Sunnah theologians, logicians, and thinkers, which has entered Islamic curricula.
العلوم العقلية (al-ʿulūm al-ʿaqliyya): The rational sciences, the subject of the chapter on India and the rational sciences.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Debate on Rational Sciences in Islam
Author introduces the work and the debate on rational sciences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to summarize the main positions in the Islamic debate on rational sciences and identify al-Subki's critique as cited by the author.

Core Idea
The permissibility of rational sciences has been debated since the Salaf, with scholars taking positions of prohibition, permission, and reconciliation.

This lesson sets the stage for studying logic and rational sciences within the Islamic tradition. The author introduces his work by noting the vast rational heritage left by Ahl al-Sunnah scholars and the need to address the complex issues surrounding its study. He then cites Shaykh al-Islam Taqi al-Din al-Subki's critique of kalam and Greek philosophy to highlight the tension.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
The passage discusses the ruling (hukm) on occupying oneself with rational sciences ('ulum 'aqliyya). This is the core question that scholars have debated.
2
Note the three positions
The author mentions that people are divided into those who forbid, those who permit, and those who reconcile (muḥarrim, mujawwiz, muwaffiq).
These are the three classical stances.
3
Recognize the authority cited
The author cites Shaykh al-Islam Taqi al-Din al-Subki, a renowned Ash'ari scholar, known for his mastery of both rational and transmitted sciences.
Al-Subki's opinion carries weight due to his expertise.
4
Understand al-Subki's claim
Al-Subki said: 'Nothing is more harmful to creeds than two things: kalam and Greek philosophy.' This is a strong warning against these rational sciences.
This quote is from his refutation of Ibn al-Qayyim's Nuniyyah.
5
Contextualize the critique
Al-Subki himself was a master of rational sciences, so his critique is not from ignorance but from concerned expertise. He also notes that theologians split into three groups, with Ash'ariyya not letting reason overcome revelation.
This shows the nuanced position within Ash'arism.

Explanation of Bahr al-Ulum on Sullam al-Ulum. Clearly, that is known by one who knows the Indian Muslim community without doubt. The talk about India is multifaceted; we present from it what we need when presenting this book to the masses of readers and intellectuals, to learn about something concerning the civilizational, intellectual, and religious condition there. Likewise, scientific activity in Islamic societies needs analysis and detail; for indeed expansion and development have occurred in it, and in later times things have been added to it that were foreign to the spirit of Islam from the branches of science, and from the arts and knowledge that only the people of a certain religion, sect, group, or innovation practiced, opposing the methodology of the people of Islam and the doctrine of Ahl al-Sunnah. Until the matter reached the point that we have a huge quantity of rational heritage left by the men of Ahl al-Sunnah, the theologians, logicians, and thinkers, and it entered the curricula of study in mosque study circles and halls of international universities, from the east of the Islamic lands to their west, so it is necessary to talk about this topic and give a brief indication to solving some of the complex problem that arose from this development. This is the general introduction to the chapter on India and the rational sciences. We will cover its details in the following chapters and sections. 16. Islam and Rational Sciences. Chapter One: Islam and Rational Sciences. First Section: The Ruling on Occupying Oneself with Rational Sciences. The discussion on this issue is not at all new; rather it is a topic that many scholars and thinkers have researched and considered, from the time of the Salaf until now, and people regarding it are among those who forbid, those who permit, and those who reconcile. The problematic was not so simple that it could be solved with one word, like 'permissible' or 'not permissible'; rather, the verified scholars, whose speech has no stumble, whose words varied on this topic, circled around it and employed skill in presenting and discussing it. Look at Shaykh al-Islam Taqi al-Din al-Subki, known for his sharpness in Ash'arism, the ocean of rational sciences, encompassing transmitted knowledge. He says in the context of refuting Ibn al-Qayyim's Nuniyyah, the gist of which is (1): 'Nothing is more harmful to creeds than two things: kalam and Greek philosophy...' And the theologians split into three sects: the Mu'tazila, the Hashawiyya, and a third, the Ash'ariyya, which did not let reason overcome revelation... In their speech... (1) I have quoted his text, may Allah have mercy on him, in a detailed research of mine entitled 'The Meaning of the Imam's Speech in Censure of Occupying Oneself with Kalam', and it has been appended to the introduction of my edition of the book al-Risala al-Tas'iniyya fi al-Usul al-Diniyya by Imam al-Safi al-Hindi, so see there: 8-27, and also see Muqaddimat al-Murashid: 25-37. 17.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is the front matter of the commentary 'Bahr al-Ulum' on 'Sullam al-Ulum'. The author begins by explaining the context of the work, particularly the significance of the Indian subcontinent within the Islamic intellectual tradition. He notes that rational sciences have expanded and sometimes incorporated elements foreign to Islam. He then introduces the central issue: the ruling on engaging with rational sciences such as kalam (theology) and logic. He mentions that this debate is longstanding, with scholars taking positions of prohibition, permission, or reconciliation. The author then cites Taqi al-Din al-Subki, a prominent Ash'ari scholar, who in refuting Ibn al-Qayyim stated that nothing is more harmful to Islamic creed than kalam and Greek philosophy. Al-Subki also notes that theologians (mutakallimun) split into three groups: Mu'tazila, Hashawiyya, and Ash'ariyya. This sets up the broader discussion that will follow in the book. The footnote indicates the author's own research on the topic.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Taj al-Din al-Subki's Conditions for Studying Logic
Conditions for studying logic and defense of al-Ghazali and al-Razi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conditions set by Taj al-Din al-Subki for studying logic and explain why al-Ghazali and al-Razi are exceptions.

Core Idea
Logic is permissible only for those whose faith is unshakable and who do not mix it with Islamic discourse.

This passage addresses a critical methodological question: when is it permissible for a Muslim scholar to study logic and philosophy? Taj al-Din al-Subki provides a clear ruling with two conditions, and the author defends the engagement of al-Ghazali and al-Razi with these sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three options
The author asks whether we should ignore intellectual sciences, open the door to everyone, or find a middle path. Locate these three options at the start of the passage.
2
Extract Subki's ruling on logic
Subki says logic is forbidden for those not grounded in Sharia, but permissible for those who have reached a high level of religious knowledge and confidence.
3
List the two conditions for permissibility
Condition 1: certainty that faith cannot be shaken by doubts. Condition 2: not mixing philosophical speech with Islamic scholarship. Find these in the passage.
4
Analyze the objection and response
The objection: al-Ghazali and al-Razi mixed philosophy with theology. The response: they were exceptional imams who had reached the highest station, so they are not to be blamed.
5
Apply the ruling to the Indian context
The author notes that in India, Ash'ari thought is mixed with philosophy, and he reaffirms that the authentic Ash'ari method is free from deviation.
