وحال علم الأصول - أصول الفقه - لا تختلف عما ذكرنا، وقد امتلأت بطون كتب الأصول بالآراء والمباحث المتعلقة بالعلوم العقلية والمنطقية، ومن أبرز الأمثلة على ذلك مقدمة «المستصفى» للإمام الغزالي ومقدمة «مختصر المنتهى الأصولي» لابن الحاجب. كما أن الفقه أيضا ما استطاع أن ينفلت من قبضة هذا التأثر، وكيف يمكنه ذلك، ونصفُ الفقه القياس، إن لم يكن كله، والقياس ـ في الصورة التي تطور إليها على أيدي علماء الأصول ـ يعتمد على أدق تفاصيل المنطق والفلسفة. ثم للإمام فخر الدين الرازي دور كبير في تطوير العلوم العقلية: فلسفة ومنطقا وكلاما وهو صاحب مدرسة فيها تتميز بمميزات وخصائص، جرى على إثره أمة من أهل العلم كالبيضاوي والأرموي والإيجي، كما لقي بعض آرائه واتجاهاته نقدا ورفضا من قبل طائفة أخرى. وما تركه الرازي من المؤلفات، كـ «الملخص و المحصل» و«المباحث المشرقية» ونهاية العقول» و شرح الإشارات» وغيرها يمثل مرحلة فارقة في طريق التطور.
The condition of the science of principles - usul al-fiqh - is no different from what we mentioned. The volumes of usul books are filled with opinions and investigations related to rational and logical sciences. Among the most prominent examples are the introduction of 'al-Mustasfa' by Imam al-Ghazali and the introduction of 'Mukhtasar al-Muntaha al-Usuli' by Ibn al-Hajib. Likewise, fiqh itself could not escape the grip of this influence; how could it, when half of fiqh is qiyas (analogy), if not all of it, and qiyas - in the form it developed in the hands of usul scholars - depends on the finest details of logic and philosophy. Then Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi played a great role in developing the rational sciences: philosophy, logic, and kalam. He was the founder of a school with distinct characteristics, followed by a multitude of scholars such as al-Baydawi, al-Urmawi, and al-Iji. Some of his views and orientations were criticized and rejected by another group. The works he left, such as 'al-Mulakhkhas', 'al-Muhassal', 'al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya', 'Nihayat al-Uqul', 'Sharh al-Isharat', and others, represent a turning point in the path of development.

Commentary
This passage continues the historical narrative, now focusing on usul al-fiqh and the pivotal role of Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. The author states that usul al-fiqh is saturated with rational and logical discussions, citing the introductions of al-Ghazali's al-Mustasfa and Ibn al-Hajib's Mukhtasar al-Muntaha as examples. Fiqh itself relies heavily on qiyas (analogical reasoning), and the refined form of qiyas developed by usul scholars is deeply grounded in logic and philosophy. The author then highlights al-Razi's contributions: he advanced philosophy, logic, and kalam, establishing a school followed by notable figures like al-Baydawi, al-Urmawi, and al-Iji, though also faced criticism. Al-Razi's major works (listed) marked a transformative stage in the integration of rational sciences into Islamic thought. This passage underscores that logic is not an alien discipline but integral to the core Islamic sciences.

Author credits al-Tusi and later scholars for integrating logic into kalam.

Learning Objective

Al-Tusi's Tajrid al-I'tiqad made logic and kalam one discipline.

This passage explains how Nasir al-Din al-Tusi's work 'Tajrid al-I'tiqad' was a turning point in Islamic intellectual history. It blended philosophy and kalam completely and introduced a logical arrangement that later theologians followed. The Systematic vs Anarchic Dichotomy in Islamic Thought
Author introduces the systematic vs anarchic dichotomy.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
The struggle between order and anarchy is ancient; Islam represents the ideal systematic order.

In this passage, the author sets the stage by presenting a universal historical dichotomy: people are divided into those who uphold order (systematic) and those who embrace anarchy. He uses the conflict between Socrates and the Sophists as an example, but then applies it to Islamic context, identifying Ahl al-Sunnah as the systematic ones and various sects as anarchic. Understanding this dichotomy helps us appreciate why logic, as a tool for order, is defended.

The author places Ahl al-Sunnah as systematic and various sects as anarchic.

الإسلام والعلوم العقلية
إن انقسام الناس إلى نظاميين وفوضويين ظاهرة قديمة قدم تاريخ الإنسان، ومن أراد الالتزام بالقيم العالية تمسك بقواعد تضمن له إثبات هذه القيم، ومن أراد الفوضى يهدم كل قاعدة توصل إلى نظام الحياة الإنسانية والكونية ويدمرها كليا وما حدث لسقراط مع السوفسطائيين في بلاد اليونان خير ما يذكر في هذا الصدام بين النظاميين والفوضويين، فهذه إذن ظاهرة عميقة الجذور في التاريخ.

زمان .
أن
ثم إن هذه القواعد الكبرى يستطيع الإنسان إذا كان ذا موهبة فكرية عالية ينفخ فيها طاقاته الفكرية الجبارة، فيتكون بذلك لون جديد من المنهج، قد يصيب الخلل والخطأُ جانبا أو أكثر من جوانبها، وبالفعل قد قامت أنواع
Islam and the Intellectual Sciences. Indeed, the division of people into systematic and anarchic is a phenomenon as old as human history. Whoever wants to adhere to lofty values clings to rules that guarantee him the affirmation of these values, and whoever wants anarchy destroys every rule that leads to a system of human and cosmic life and destroys it completely. What happened to Socrates with the Sophists in the land of Greece is the best example to mention in this clash between the systematic and the anarchic. So this is a deeply rooted phenomenon in history. What we mean by logic here is nothing but a method of deduction and proof, followed by the scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah throughout the ages, whether you call it Aristotelian, Stoic, Illuminative, or other names that come to your mind. I mean specifically that category of scholars known in our custom as the mutakallimun (theologians), starting from Imam al-Ghazali and after him. The jurists and usul scholars, because their deductive method ... and I do not mean that it is different from the deductive method followed by the mutakallimun, due to the difference of the two sciences. For the goal of fiqh - and thus the usul attributed to it - is not certainty, but what is required is preponderance of opinion. As for the theological method, the basis of it is attaining certainty, so the essence of their two methods agrees according to the nature of these two sciences. It is not for the theologian to cast doubt on the method of the jurists, nor for the jurists to be insolent towards the method of the theologians, as long as this difference I have pointed out is clear to everyone, if they are seekers of truth. We said that people are divided into the systematic and the anarchic, and Islam is the ideal system, according to what the majority of its people understand, and they are the Ash'arites and Maturidites. In their opposite are the tents of the people of falsehood, who have no method except resorting to anarchy, and they are peoples. Explanation of Bahr al-Ulum on Sullam al-Ulum. And various sects, some of whom are outside the circle of Islam entirely, and some entered but did not remain upright, and all want to establish falsehood and fear the dominance of truth. So they set out to destroy the values and principles that the guided nation received from Allah and His Messenger (peace be upon him) and from those who followed his guidance. So they placed their picks and axes on a ladder with steps, which the nation used to ascend to a tower with towers. This ladder is logic; the anarchists wanted to destroy it, so they first described it as Aristotelian or Greek or ..., just as one of us describes when he throws stones at a dog in the street or kills it, saying it is a mad dog that bites people, so that he can achieve what he wants easily. .. We, the community of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, believe in the correctness of our religion and our doctrines, and we are certain of the falsehood of other religions and other doctrines. And there will always remain among us - by the permission of the One who empowers those who can establish truth and abolish falsehood. And this affirmation and that negation are not dependent on the logic of Aristotle or the philosophy of Ibn Sina, as is imagined. Rather, there are rules agreed upon by all rational people, and they are the major rational principles, such as the law of identity, the law of the excluded middle, the law of the impossibility of the conjunction of two contradictories, the raising of two contradictories, and the impossibility of obtaining the obtained... They are greater than Aristotle and Plato, and older than al-Farabi and Ibn Sina. Upon them revolves the method; it cannot be doubted nor disputed, unless one descends to the level of sophistry, which no time is free of. Then, indeed, these major rules, if a person has a high intellectual talent, he can breathe into them his tremendous intellectual energies, and thus a new kind of method is formed, which may be affected by error and mistake in one or more of its aspects, and indeed, types have already emerged.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is an introductory discussion by the author of Bahr al-Ulum, setting the stage for the study of logic. The author begins by presenting a universal historical dichotomy: the division of people into those who uphold order (systematic) and those who embrace anarchy. He uses the conflict between Socrates and the Sophists as an example, portraying logic as a method of proof and deduction used by Ahl al-Sunnah scholars, especially the mutakallimun (theologians) from al-Ghazali onward. The author clarifies that he is not dismissing other groups but is specifically focusing on the method of the mutakallimun. He then distinguishes between the method of fiqh (jurisprudence) which aims at preponderance of opinion (ghalabat al-zann), and the method of kalam (theology) which aims at certainty (yaqin). Both methods are valid in their own domains, and neither should be criticized by the other. The author then identifies the ideal system as Islam as understood by the Ash'arites and Maturidites, contrasting them with the 'people of falsehood' who are anarchic. These anarchists attack logic by labeling it as Aristotelian or Greek, hoping to discredit it. The author defends logic by asserting that the fundamental rational principles (law of identity, excluded middle, non-contradiction, etc.) are universal and not dependent on any particular philosopher. They are innate to human reason and cannot be disputed except by sophists. Finally, he notes that human intellect can develop new methods based on these principles, though they may contain errors. The passage thus serves as an apologetic for the study of logic, grounding it in universal rational principles rather than a specific tradition.

Key Terms
المنطق (al-mantiq): Here defined as 'منهج استدلال وإثبات' (a method of deduction and proof) used by Ahl al-Sunnah scholars. [Note: No significant shift; stable across tradition.]
الاستدلال (al-istidlal): The process of inference or deduction leading to proof. [Note: No significant shift.]
اليقين (al-yaqin): Certainty, the goal of theological method (kalam). [Note: No significant shift.]
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Preponderance of opinion, the goal of fiqh method. [Note: No significant shift.]
القواعد العقلية (al-qawa'id al-'aqliyya): The fundamental rational principles such as law of identity, excluded middle, non-contradiction, etc., which are universal and not tied to any particular philosopher. [Note: No significant shift.]

Key Takeaway
The systematic vs anarchic dichotomy is a universal historical phenomenon; Islam represents the systematic order, and logic is its methodological tool.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
The Definition and Significance of Logic
Author defines logic and defends its universal nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-mantiq as a method of deduction and proof used by Ahl al-Sunnah and explain why it is not dependent on any particular philosopher.

Core Idea
Logic is a universal method of proof, not a Greek import.

The author defines logic simply as a method of deduction and proof. He emphasizes that this method has been used by Ahl al-Sunnah scholars throughout the ages, irrespective of labels like Aristotelian or Stoic. He then defends logic against accusations of being foreign by grounding it in universal rational principles that transcend any particular philosopher.

Guided Path
1
Extract the definition
Find the sentence where the author states 'ما نريد بالمنطق هنا إلا منهج استدلال وإثبات'. What does this definition include?
It includes both deduction (istidlal) and proof (ithbat).
2
Identify the practitioners
Who does the author say used this method? Look for 'علماء أهل السنة والجماعة' and 'المتكلمين'.
The author mentions the mutakallimun from al-Ghazali onward, as well as jurists and usul scholars.
3
Understand the defense
How does the author counter the accusation that logic is Aristotelian? Look for the mention of 'القواعد العقلية' and the list of principles.
He argues that logic is based on universal rational principles agreed upon by all rational people, not on Aristotle.
4
Analyze the implications
Why is it important that these principles are universal and agreed upon by all rational people?
It means logic is not the property of any one culture or philosopher, but a shared human heritage.

الإسلام والعلوم العقلية
إن انقسام الناس إلى نظاميين وفوضويين ظاهرة قديمة قدم تاريخ الإنسان، ومن أراد الالتزام بالقيم العالية تمسك بقواعد تضمن له إثبات هذه القيم، ومن أراد الفوضى يهدم كل قاعدة توصل إلى نظام الحياة الإنسانية والكونية ويدمرها كليا وما حدث لسقراط مع السوفسطائيين في بلاد اليونان خير ما يذكر في هذا الصدام بين النظاميين والفوضويين، فهذه إذن ظاهرة عميقة الجذور في التاريخ.
وما نريد بالمنطق هنا ليس إلا منهج استدلال وإثبات، درج عليه علماء أهل السنة والجماعة عبر العصور، سواء سميته أرسطيا أو رواقيا أو إشراقيا، أو غيرها من الأسامي التي تخطر ببالك. أريد منهم بالتحديد تلك الفئة من العلماء المعروفين في عرفنا بالمتكلمين، اعتبارا من الإمام الغزالي ومن بعده. الفقهاء والأصوليين، وذلك لأن المنهج الاستدلالي عندهم

شرح بحر العلوم على سلم العلوم
وفرق شتى، منهم من هو خارج عن دائرة الإسلام بالكلية، ومنهم من دخل، ولم يستقم ، والكل يريد إقامة الباطل ، ويخاف سيادة الحق. فانطلقوا نحو هدم القيم والمبادئ التي تلقتها الأمة المهتدية عن الله وعن رسوله صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وعمن اقتدى بهديه . فوضعوا معاولهم وفؤوسهم على سلم ذو أدراج، استخدمته الأمة لترتقي به إلى صرح ذو أبراج.
وهذا السلم هو المنطق ، أراد الفوضويون أن يهدموه، فوصفوه أولا بأنه أرسطي أو إغريقي أو ... كما يصف أحدنا حين يقذف كلبا في الطريق بالحجارة أو يقتله إنه كلب مجنون يعض الإنسان ؛ حتى يتم له ما أراد بسهولة .

-
ونحن معاشر أهل السنة والجماعة، نعتقد صحة ديننا وعقائدنا، ونجزم ببطلان غيره من الأديان وغيرها من العقائد، ولا يزال فينا - بإذن من تعهد من يقدر على إحقاق الحق وإبطال الباطل. وهذا الإثبات وذاك الإبطال ليسا متوقفين على منطق أرسطو أو فلسفة ابن سينا، كما يتوهم، بل هناك قواعد متفق عليها بين العقلاء جميعا، وهي كبرى القواعد العقلية، كقانون الذاتية، وقانون عدم الوسط، وقانون استحالة اجتماع النقيضين، وارتفاع النقيضين، واستحالة تحصيل الحاصل... وهي أكبر من أرسطو وأفلاطون، وأقدم من الفارابي وابن سينا عليها مدار المنهج لا يمكن التشكيك فيه ولا النزاع حوله، إلا إن تدنى الإنسان إلى درجة السفسطة، وهي لا يخلو منها
زمان .
أن
ثم إن هذه القواعد الكبرى يستطيع الإنسان إذا كان ذا موهبة فكرية عالية ينفخ فيها طاقاته الفكرية الجبارة، فيتكون بذلك لون جديد من المنهج، قد يصيب الخلل والخطأُ جانبا أو أكثر من جوانبها، وبالفعل قد قامت أنواع
Islam and the Intellectual Sciences. Indeed, the division of people into systematic and anarchic is a phenomenon as old as human history. Whoever wants to adhere to lofty values clings to rules that guarantee him the affirmation of these values, and whoever wants anarchy destroys every rule that leads to a system of human and cosmic life and destroys it completely. What happened to Socrates with the Sophists in the land of Greece is the best example to mention in this clash between the systematic and the anarchic. So this is a deeply rooted phenomenon in history. What we mean by logic here is nothing but a method of deduction and proof, followed by the scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah throughout the ages, whether you call it Aristotelian, Stoic, Illuminative, or other names that come to your mind. I mean specifically that category of scholars known in our custom as the mutakallimun (theologians), starting from Imam al-Ghazali and after him. The jurists and usul scholars, because their deductive method ... and I do not mean that it is different from the deductive method followed by the mutakallimun, due to the difference of the two sciences. For the goal of fiqh - and thus the usul attributed to it - is not certainty, but what is required is preponderance of opinion. As for the theological method, the basis of it is attaining certainty, so the essence of their two methods agrees according to the nature of these two sciences. It is not for the theologian to cast doubt on the method of the jurists, nor for the jurists to be insolent towards the method of the theologians, as long as this difference I have pointed out is clear to everyone, if they are seekers of truth. We said that people are divided into the systematic and the anarchic, and Islam is the ideal system, according to what the majority of its people understand, and they are the Ash'arites and Maturidites. In their opposite are the tents of the people of falsehood, who have no method except resorting to anarchy, and they are peoples. Explanation of Bahr al-Ulum on Sullam al-Ulum. And various sects, some of whom are outside the circle of Islam entirely, and some entered but did not remain upright, and all want to establish falsehood and fear the dominance of truth. So they set out to destroy the values and principles that the guided nation received from Allah and His Messenger (peace be upon him) and from those who followed his guidance. So they placed their picks and axes on a ladder with steps, which the nation used to ascend to a tower with towers. This ladder is logic; the anarchists wanted to destroy it, so they first described it as Aristotelian or Greek or ..., just as one of us describes when he throws stones at a dog in the street or kills it, saying it is a mad dog that bites people, so that he can achieve what he wants easily. .. We, the community of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, believe in the correctness of our religion and our doctrines, and we are certain of the falsehood of other religions and other doctrines. And there will always remain among us - by the permission of the One who empowers those who can establish truth and abolish falsehood. And this affirmation and that negation are not dependent on the logic of Aristotle or the philosophy of Ibn Sina, as is imagined. Rather, there are rules agreed upon by all rational people, and they are the major rational principles, such as the law of identity, the law of the excluded middle, the law of the impossibility of the conjunction of two contradictories, the raising of two contradictories, and the impossibility of obtaining the obtained... They are greater than Aristotle and Plato, and older than al-Farabi and Ibn Sina. Upon them revolves the method; it cannot be doubted nor disputed, unless one descends to the level of sophistry, which no time is free of. Then, indeed, these major rules, if a person has a high intellectual talent, he can breathe into them his tremendous intellectual energies, and thus a new kind of method is formed, which may be affected by error and mistake in one or more of its aspects, and indeed, types have already emerged.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is an introductory discussion by the author of Bahr al-Ulum, setting the stage for the study of logic. The author begins by presenting a universal historical dichotomy: the division of people into those who uphold order (systematic) and those who embrace anarchy. He uses the conflict between Socrates and the Sophists as an example, portraying logic as a method of proof and deduction used by Ahl al-Sunnah scholars, especially the mutakallimun (theologians) from al-Ghazali onward. The author clarifies that he is not dismissing other groups but is specifically focusing on the method of the mutakallimun. He then distinguishes between the method of fiqh (jurisprudence) which aims at preponderance of opinion (ghalabat al-zann), and the method of kalam (theology) which aims at certainty (yaqin). Both methods are valid in their own domains, and neither should be criticized by the other. The author then identifies the ideal system as Islam as understood by the Ash'arites and Maturidites, contrasting them with the 'people of falsehood' who are anarchic. These anarchists attack logic by labeling it as Aristotelian or Greek, hoping to discredit it. The author defends logic by asserting that the fundamental rational principles (law of identity, excluded middle, non-contradiction, etc.) are universal and not dependent on any particular philosopher. They are innate to human reason and cannot be disputed except by sophists. Finally, he notes that human intellect can develop new methods based on these principles, though they may contain errors. The passage thus serves as an apologetic for the study of logic, grounding it in universal rational principles rather than a specific tradition.

Key Terms
المنطق (al-mantiq): Here defined as 'منهج استدلال وإثبات' (a method of deduction and proof) used by Ahl al-Sunnah scholars. [Note: No significant shift; stable across tradition.]
الاستدلال (al-istidlal): The process of inference or deduction leading to proof. [Note: No significant shift.]
اليقين (al-yaqin): Certainty, the goal of theological method (kalam). [Note: No significant shift.]
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Preponderance of opinion, the goal of fiqh method. [Note: No significant shift.]
القواعد العقلية (al-qawa'id al-'aqliyya): The fundamental rational principles such as law of identity, excluded middle, non-contradiction, etc., which are universal and not tied to any particular philosopher. [Note: No significant shift.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Aristotle's teachings
B) Universal agreement of all rational people
C) Islamic revelation only
D) The Ash'arite school

Key Takeaway
Logic, defined as a method of deduction, is rooted in universal rational principles that are innate to human reason and not the property of any one philosophical tradition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Write a short argument using the law of non-contradiction to refute a claim that contradicts a clear Islamic principle. For example, if someone says 'God is both one and many', show why that is impossible.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
The Epistemological Distinction between Fiqh and Kalam
Author distinguishes epistemic goals of fiqh and kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the epistemic goals of fiqh (preponderance of opinion) and kalam (certainty) and explain why both methods are valid in their own domains.

Core Idea
Fiqh seeks preponderance, kalam seeks certainty; each method is valid within its own scope.

The author makes a crucial distinction between the method of fiqh (jurisprudence) and that of kalam (theology). Fiqh aims at 'ghalabat al-zann' (preponderance of opinion), while kalam aims at 'al-yaqin' (certainty). He warns against mutual criticism by practitioners of each science, emphasizing that their methods differ due to the nature of their respective subjects. Understanding this distinction prevents methodological confusion and promotes respect between scholars of different disciplines.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sciences
Find where the author mentions 'الفقه' and 'المنهج الكلامي'. What are their respective goals?
Fiqh aims at preponderance of opinion (ghalabat al-zann), kalam aims at certainty (yaqin).
2
Note the epistemic terms
Look for 'اليقين' and 'غلبة الظن'. Write down their definitions.
Yaqin is certainty, ghalabat al-zann is preponderance of opinion.
3
Understand the reason for difference
According to the author, why do the methods differ? Look for 'لاختلاف العلمين'.
The difference stems from the nature of the two sciences: fiqh deals with practical matters where certainty is not always possible, while kalam deals with foundational beliefs requiring certainty.
4
Extract the author's warning
What does the author say about theologians criticizing jurists and vice versa? What is the condition for mutual respect?
He says each should not criticize the other's method, provided they understand the difference and are seekers of truth.

This ladder is logic; the anarchists wanted to destroy it, so they first described it as Aristotelian or Greek or ..., just as one of us describes when he throws stones at a dog in the street or kills it, saying it is a mad dog that bites people, so that he can achieve what he wants easily. .. We, the community of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, believe in the correctness of our religion and our doctrines, and we are certain of the falsehood of other religions and other doctrines. And there will always remain among us - by the permission of the One who empowers those who can establish truth and abolish falsehood. And this affirmation and that negation are not dependent on the logic of Aristotle or the philosophy of Ibn Sina, as is imagined. Rather, there are rules agreed upon by all rational people, and they are the major rational principles, such as the law of identity, the law of the excluded middle, the law of the impossibility of the conjunction of two contradictories, the raising of two contradictories, and the impossibility of obtaining the obtained... They are greater than Aristotle and Plato, and older than al-Farabi and Ibn Sina. Upon them revolves the method; it cannot be doubted nor disputed, unless one descends to the level of sophistry, which no time is free of. Then, indeed, these major rules, if a person has a high intellectual talent, he can breathe into them his tremendous intellectual energies, and thus a new kind of method is formed, which may be affected by error and mistake in one or more of its aspects, and indeed, types have already emerged.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is an introductory discussion by the author of Bahr al-Ulum, setting the stage for the study of logic. The author begins by presenting a universal historical dichotomy: the division of people into those who uphold order (systematic) and those who embrace anarchy. He uses the conflict between Socrates and the Sophists as an example, portraying logic as a method of proof and deduction used by Ahl al-Sunnah scholars, especially the mutakallimun (theologians) from al-Ghazali onward. The author clarifies that he is not dismissing other groups but is specifically focusing on the method of the mutakallimun. He then distinguishes between the method of fiqh (jurisprudence) which aims at preponderance of opinion (ghalabat al-zann), and the method of kalam (theology) which aims at certainty (yaqin). Both methods are valid in their own domains, and neither should be criticized by the other. The author then identifies the ideal system as Islam as understood by the Ash'arites and Maturidites, contrasting them with the 'people of falsehood' who are anarchic. These anarchists attack logic by labeling it as Aristotelian or Greek, hoping to discredit it. The author defends logic by asserting that the fundamental rational principles (law of identity, excluded middle, non-contradiction, etc.) are universal and not dependent on any particular philosopher. They are innate to human reason and cannot be disputed except by sophists. Finally, he notes that human intellect can develop new methods based on these principles, though they may contain errors. The passage thus serves as an apologetic for the study of logic, grounding it in universal rational principles rather than a specific tradition.

Key Terms
المنطق (al-mantiq): Here defined as 'منهج استدلال وإثبات' (a method of deduction and proof) used by Ahl al-Sunnah scholars. [Note: No significant shift; stable across tradition.]
الاستدلال (al-istidlal): The process of inference or deduction leading to proof. [Note: No significant shift.]
اليقين (al-yaqin): Certainty, the goal of theological method (kalam). [Note: No significant shift.]
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Preponderance of opinion, the goal of fiqh method. [Note: No significant shift.]
القواعد العقلية (al-qawa'id al-'aqliyya): The fundamental rational principles such as law of identity, excluded middle, non-contradiction, etc., which are universal and not tied to any particular philosopher. [Note: No significant shift.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the goal of the theological method (المنهج الكلامي)?
A) Preponderance of opinion
B) Certainty
C) Practical application
D) Both certainty and preponderance

Key Takeaway
Fiqh aims at preponderance of opinion, kalam aims at certainty; each method is valid in its own domain and should not be criticized from the other's perspective.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take a legal ruling (e.g., the prohibition of riba) and a theological doctrine (e.g., the oneness of God). Explain why the method used to establish each differs in terms of epistemic certainty.
?
Imagine a debate between a jurist and a theologian. Write a short exchange where the theologian demands certainty for a fiqh ruling, and the jurist responds using the author's reasoning to defend the validity of preponderance.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Logic as an Islamic Ladder: Defending the Tool
Author defends logic against critics and introduces universal rational principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the author defends logic against the anarchists and identify the universal rational principles that form the foundation of truth.

Core Idea
Logic is a tool, not the source of truth; truth rests on universal rational principles agreed upon by all rational people.

In this opening passage, the commentator of Sullam al-Ulum sets the stage for studying logic by defending it against those who would demolish it. He likens logic to a ladder used by the Muslim community to ascend to knowledge. He emphasizes that the truth of Islam is not dependent on Aristotelian logic but on universal rational principles that are pre-Islamic and pre-Aristotelian.

Guided Path
1
Identify the metaphor for logic
Find the simile used: logic is a ladder (sullam) with steps that the Muslim community uses to ascend to a lofty structure of knowledge.
This metaphor highlights logic as a facilitating tool, not an end in itself.
2
Recognize the anarchists' strategy
The anarchists (al-fawdawiyyun) attack logic by first labeling it as foreign (Aristotelian, Greek) to discredit it, analogous to calling a dog mad before killing it.
This is an ad hominem tactic, not a substantive critique.
3
Extract the universal rational principles
List the principles mentioned: law of identity, law of non-contradiction, impossibility of conjunction of two contradictories, impossibility of simultaneous negation of two contradictories, impossibility of obtaining the already obtained.
These are foundational and agreed upon by all rational people, independent of any specific logical system.
4
Understand the claim about truth
The author asserts that the truth of Islamic beliefs does not depend on the soundness of Aristotelian logic or Avicennan philosophy; it is grounded in the universal rational principles.
Thus, even if all Aristotelian logic were invalid, the truth of Islam remains intact.

الإسلام والعلوم العقلية

السفسطة .
من
وليس منهجنا هو الاستدلال أولا، ثم الاعتقاد، وهو منهج فلسفي، بل نحن معاشر متكلمي أهل السنة نعتقد أولا ثم نستدل، فإذا تبين بطلان دليل فرضا فإنه لا يعني بالضرورة أن المدلول في حد ذاته باطل، طالما يستحيل
Commentary Bahr al-Ulum on Sullam al-Ulum. And various factions, among them those who are completely outside the circle of Islam, and among them those who entered but did not remain upright, and all of them desire to establish falsehood and fear the dominance of truth. So they launched towards demolishing the values and principles that the guided nation received from Allah and His Messenger, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and from those who followed his guidance. So they placed their pickaxes and axes on a ladder with steps, which the nation used to ascend to a lofty structure. And this ladder is logic. The anarchists wanted to demolish it, so they first described it as Aristotelian or Greek or... just as one of us describes when he throws stones at a dog in the road or kills it, saying it is a mad dog that bites people, so that he may easily achieve what he wants. - And we, the community of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, believe in the correctness of our religion and our doctrines, and we are certain of the falsehood of other religions and other beliefs, and there still remains among us, by permission of the One who has taken charge, those who are able to establish truth and refute falsehood. And this establishment and that refutation are not dependent on Aristotle's logic or Ibn Sina's philosophy, as is imagined. Rather, there are rules agreed upon by all rational people, and they are the major rational principles, such as the law of identity, the law of non-contradiction, the law of impossibility of the conjunction of two contradictories, and of their simultaneous negation, and the impossibility of obtaining the already obtained... They are greater than Aristotle and Plato, and older than al-Farabi and Ibn Sina. The methodology revolves around them; it cannot be doubted or disputed, unless a person descends to the level of sophistry, which is never absent from any time. Then indeed, these major principles, if a person has a high intellectual talent, he can blow into them his tremendous intellectual energies, thereby a new type of methodology is formed, which may be affected by error and mistake in one or more of its aspects. And indeed, various types of these methodologies have emerged from Islam and the rational sciences, the most important of which is what we call Aristotelian logic. It has received admiration from many and also faced criticism from many. There is no harm in any of that. The Imams of Islam also noticed what in this Greek heritage - whether it is from Aristotle or not - contradicts the doctrines of Islam, and they explained its falsehood, and most of that was related to metaphysical investigations. However, his logic also was connected to that metaphysics, such as the belief in causality between genus and differentia and so on. There still remain among us those who point out the corruption of what is corrupt in it. And it has been the practice of the speculative theologians (mutakallimun) for centuries to use this type of methodology known as logic, many of whose rules are attributed to Aristotle, sometimes our scholars agree with him and sometimes they disagree. However, there is no doubt that this logic has been widely used in demonstrating the correctness of much of what we believe and refuting the doctrines of the people of falsehood. And what the anarchists want when they direct their arrows of criticism at this logic is nothing but the demolition of what this logic has been used for; because they are anarchists, and it is nothing but the spread of sophistry. Hence, this tribulation must be confronted with all determination and seriousness. The truth we believe is true in itself, and our predecessors have established it, and if Allah wills, we will establish it before whomever wants, whoever they may be. The soundness of certainty and the correctness of belief are never dependent on the soundness of Aristotelian logic. And the falsehood we reject is false in itself, and our scholars have refuted it with the worst of refutations, and by Allah's permission we are able to do that in any place. And our methodology is not first to infer and then to believe—that is a philosophical methodology. Rather, we, the community of speculative theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah, believe first and then infer. So if the falsehood of a proof becomes apparent hypothetically, it does not necessarily mean that the thing proved is in itself false, as long as it is impossible...
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is an introductory defense of the study of logic within the Islamic tradition, written by the commentator of Sullam al-'Ulum. The commentator begins by describing various factions that oppose Islam and seek to demolish its values. They target logic, which is likened to a ladder used by the Muslim community to ascend to higher knowledge. The anarchists (fawdawiyyun) attempt to discredit logic by labeling it as foreign (Aristotelian or Greek), similar to someone killing a dog by first calling it mad. The commentator then affirms the stance of Ahl al-Sunnah: they are certain of the truth of Islam and the falsehood of other beliefs. Importantly, this certainty does not depend on Aristotelian logic or Avicennan philosophy. Instead, there are universal rational principles (al-qawa'id al-'aqliyya al-kubra) agreed upon by all rational people, such as the law of non-contradiction and the law of identity. These principles are pre-Aristotelian and pre-Islamic; they form the foundation of any sound methodology. However, from these principles, various methodologies can be developed, and one of them is Aristotelian logic. This logic has been used by Muslim scholars to defend Islamic doctrines, though it has also been criticized. The commentator emphasizes that the truth of Islam is self-evident and not contingent on the validity of Aristotelian logic. The methodology of the mutakallimun is to believe first and then infer, unlike philosophers who infer first and then believe. Therefore, if a particular proof for a belief is found to be flawed, it does not necessarily invalidate the belief itself, provided the belief is impossible to be false. The passage thus serves to justify the use of logic as a tool while reaffirming the primacy of faith and the independence of Islamic truth from any particular logical system.

Key Terms
المنطق (al-mantiq): In this passage, logic is defined as a ladder (sullam) used by the Muslim community to ascend to higher knowledge, and specifically identified with Aristotelian logic as a methodological tool. [Note: No significant shift in this passage; it refers to the standard definition of logic as a tool for correct reasoning.]
القواعد العقلية (al-qawa'id al-'aqliyya): Universal rational principles such as the law of identity and non-contradiction, which are foundational and agreed upon by all rational people, independent of any specific logical system. [Note: These are often referred to as 'primary intelligibles' (awwaliyyat) in later texts; here they are called 'major rational principles'.]
الفوضويون (al-fawdawiyyun): Those who seek to demolish the values and principles of Islam, specifically targeting logic as a means to undermine Islamic scholarship. [Note: This term is used polemically in this text; it is not a standard technical term in logic.]
السفسطة (al-safsata): Sophistry, the lowest level of reasoning where one denies the basic rational principles, leading to skepticism and denial of truth. [Note: This term is synonymous with 'sophistical' fallacies in Aristotelian logic, but here it denotes a complete rejection of rational principles.]
المتكلمون (al-mutakallimun): The speculative theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah who prioritize belief (i'tiqad) over inference (istidlal), using logic only after affirming doctrine. [Note: This is a standard term for Islamic theologians; the emphasis on 'believe first then infer' is methodological and distinct from philosophers.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, on what is the truth of Islam dependent?
A) The validity of Aristotelian syllogisms
B) The universal rational principles independent of Aristotle
C) The consensus of the Muslim community
D) The works of Ibn Sina

Key Takeaway
Islamic truth is founded on universal rational principles (like non-contradiction) that are more foundational than any specific logical system, such as Aristotelian logic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
List the universal rational principles explicitly mentioned in the passage (e.g., law of identity, law of non-contradiction). For each principle, think of a simple Islamic theological example that implicitly uses it.
?
Explain in your own words why the author claims that Islamic truth does not depend on Aristotelian logic. Use the metaphor of the ladder to illustrate.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
5 min
Sunni Method: Believe First, Then Infer
Author explains the methodology of Ahl al-Sunnah: believe first, then infer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the methodology of Ahl al-Sunnah (believe first, then infer) from the philosophical methodology and explain its implications for theological proofs.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunnah start with belief, not proof; a flawed proof does not make the belief false.

The commentator explains the distinctive methodology of the mutakallimun of Ahl al-Sunnah. Unlike philosophers who first establish proofs and then derive beliefs, Sunni theologians hold their beliefs first, and then use logic and inference to support them. This means that if a specific proof is found to be flawed, the belief itself remains valid, because its truth is independently established through revelation and the universal rational principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two methodologies
Contrast the philosophical method: 'infer first, then believe' with the Sunni method: 'believe first, then infer'. The passage explicitly states: 'Our methodology is not first to infer and then to believe—that is a philosophical methodology. Rather, we believe first and then infer.'
This is a fundamental epistemological difference between philosophers and mutakallimun.
2
Understand the consequence of a flawed proof
If a proof (dalil) used to support a belief is found to be false, the Sunni methodology dictates that the belief itself is not necessarily false. Because the belief is held on independent grounds (e.g., revelation, fitra), the proof is merely a supporting tool.
This protects Islamic doctrines from being vulnerable to errors in discursive reasoning.
3
Connect to universal rational principles
The author earlier emphasized that truth is grounded in universal rational principles and revelation, not in any particular logical system. Thus, even if a logical argument for a belief fails, the belief may still be true in itself.
The believer's certainty (yaqin) comes from a source beyond human logic.
4
Reflect on the practical implication
When engaging in theological debate (jadal), a Sunni mutakallim can confidently argue for his beliefs without fear that a refutation of his argument destroys the belief itself. He can always fall back on the independent truth of the belief.
This methodology allows for robust defense of faith while using rational tools critically.

الإسلام والعلوم العقلية
تلك المناهج ، من أهمها ما نسميه المنطق الأرسطي، ولقي إعجاب الكثيرين، وتعرض لنقد الكثيرين أيضا. ولا غضاضة في شيء من ذلك. وأئمة الإسلام أيضا تنبهوا إلى ما في هذا التراث اليوناني - سواء هو لأرسطو أو لا - مما يخالف عقائد الإسلام، وبينوا بطلان ذلك، وكان أكثره فيما يتعلق بالمباحث الميتافيزيقية، إلا أن منطقه أيضا كان يمت إلى تلك الميتافيزيقا بصلة، كاعتقاد العلية بين الجنس والفصل وما إلى ذلك، لم يزل فينا من ينبه على فساد الفاسد فيه .
ومما اعتاده العلماء المتكلمون منذ القرون استخدام هذا اللون من المنهج المعروف بالمنطق، الكثير من قواعده منسوب إلى أرسطو، قد يوافقه عليه علمائنا وقد يخالفونه إلا أن مما لا شك فيه أن هذا المنطق استخدم استخداما عريضا في بيان صحة كثير مما نعتقده، وإبطالِ مذاهب أهل الباطل. والذي يريده الفوضويون حين يوجهون سهام النقد إلى هذا المنطق ليس إلا هدم ما استخدم فيه هذا المنطق؛ لأنهم فوضويون، وليس إلا نشر ومن هنا يجب التصدي لهذه الفتنة بكل عزم وجدية، والحق الذي نعتقده حق في نفسه، وقد أثبته ،سلفنا ، وإن شاء الله سنثبته عند من يريد، كائنا كان ، وبرد اليقين وصحة المعتقد ليس متوقفا على سلامة المنطق الأرسطي أبدا، والباطل الذي نرفضه باطل في نفسه، وقد أبطله علمائنا شر إبطال، وبإذن الله نقدر على ذلك في أي مكان كان .
السفسطة .
من
وليس منهجنا هو الاستدلال أولا، ثم الاعتقاد، وهو منهج فلسفي، بل نحن معاشر متكلمي أهل السنة نعتقد أولا ثم نستدل، فإذا تبين بطلان دليل فرضا فإنه لا يعني بالضرورة أن المدلول في حد ذاته باطل، طالما يستحيل
Commentary Bahr al-Ulum on Sullam al-Ulum. And various factions, among them those who are completely outside the circle of Islam, and among them those who entered but did not remain upright, and all of them desire to establish falsehood and fear the dominance of truth. So they launched towards demolishing the values and principles that the guided nation received from Allah and His Messenger, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and from those who followed his guidance. So they placed their pickaxes and axes on a ladder with steps, which the nation used to ascend to a lofty structure. And this ladder is logic. The anarchists wanted to demolish it, so they first described it as Aristotelian or Greek or... just as one of us describes when he throws stones at a dog in the road or kills it, saying it is a mad dog that bites people, so that he may easily achieve what he wants. - And we, the community of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, believe in the correctness of our religion and our doctrines, and we are certain of the falsehood of other religions and other beliefs, and there still remains among us, by permission of the One who has taken charge, those who are able to establish truth and refute falsehood. And this establishment and that refutation are not dependent on Aristotle's logic or Ibn Sina's philosophy, as is imagined. Rather, there are rules agreed upon by all rational people, and they are the major rational principles, such as the law of identity, the law of non-contradiction, the law of impossibility of the conjunction of two contradictories, and of their simultaneous negation, and the impossibility of obtaining the already obtained... They are greater than Aristotle and Plato, and older than al-Farabi and Ibn Sina. The methodology revolves around them; it cannot be doubted or disputed, unless a person descends to the level of sophistry, which is never absent from any time. Then indeed, these major principles, if a person has a high intellectual talent, he can blow into them his tremendous intellectual energies, thereby a new type of methodology is formed, which may be affected by error and mistake in one or more of its aspects. And indeed, various types of these methodologies have emerged from Islam and the rational sciences, the most important of which is what we call Aristotelian logic. It has received admiration from many and also faced criticism from many. There is no harm in any of that. The Imams of Islam also noticed what in this Greek heritage - whether it is from Aristotle or not - contradicts the doctrines of Islam, and they explained its falsehood, and most of that was related to metaphysical investigations. However, his logic also was connected to that metaphysics, such as the belief in causality between genus and differentia and so on. There still remain among us those who point out the corruption of what is corrupt in it. And it has been the practice of the speculative theologians (mutakallimun) for centuries to use this type of methodology known as logic, many of whose rules are attributed to Aristotle, sometimes our scholars agree with him and sometimes they disagree. However, there is no doubt that this logic has been widely used in demonstrating the correctness of much of what we believe and refuting the doctrines of the people of falsehood. And what the anarchists want when they direct their arrows of criticism at this logic is nothing but the demolition of what this logic has been used for; because they are anarchists, and it is nothing but the spread of sophistry. Hence, this tribulation must be confronted with all determination and seriousness. The truth we believe is true in itself, and our predecessors have established it, and if Allah wills, we will establish it before whomever wants, whoever they may be. The soundness of certainty and the correctness of belief are never dependent on the soundness of Aristotelian logic. And the falsehood we reject is false in itself, and our scholars have refuted it with the worst of refutations, and by Allah's permission we are able to do that in any place. And our methodology is not first to infer and then to believe—that is a philosophical methodology. Rather, we, the community of speculative theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah, believe first and then infer. So if the falsehood of a proof becomes apparent hypothetically, it does not necessarily mean that the thing proved is in itself false, as long as it is impossible...
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is an introductory defense of the study of logic within the Islamic tradition, written by the commentator of Sullam al-'Ulum. The commentator begins by describing various factions that oppose Islam and seek to demolish its values. They target logic, which is likened to a ladder used by the Muslim community to ascend to higher knowledge. The anarchists (fawdawiyyun) attempt to discredit logic by labeling it as foreign (Aristotelian or Greek), similar to someone killing a dog by first calling it mad. The commentator then affirms the stance of Ahl al-Sunnah: they are certain of the truth of Islam and the falsehood of other beliefs. Importantly, this certainty does not depend on Aristotelian logic or Avicennan philosophy. Instead, there are universal rational principles (al-qawa'id al-'aqliyya al-kubra) agreed upon by all rational people, such as the law of non-contradiction and the law of identity. These principles are pre-Aristotelian and pre-Islamic; they form the foundation of any sound methodology. However, from these principles, various methodologies can be developed, and one of them is Aristotelian logic. This logic has been used by Muslim scholars to defend Islamic doctrines, though it has also been criticized. The commentator emphasizes that the truth of Islam is self-evident and not contingent on the validity of Aristotelian logic. The methodology of the mutakallimun is to believe first and then infer, unlike philosophers who infer first and then believe. Therefore, if a particular proof for a belief is found to be flawed, it does not necessarily invalidate the belief itself, provided the belief is impossible to be false. The passage thus serves to justify the use of logic as a tool while reaffirming the primacy of faith and the independence of Islamic truth from any particular logical system.

Key Terms
المتكلمون (al-mutakallimun): The speculative theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah who prioritize belief (i'tiqad) over inference (istidlal), using logic only after affirming doctrine. [Note: This is a standard term for Islamic theologians; the emphasis on 'believe first then infer' is methodological and distinct from philosophers.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the methodological principle of Ahl al-Sunnah?
A) Infer first, then believe
B) Neither belief nor inference; only revelation
C) Believe first, then infer
D) Only inference, no belief required

Key Takeaway
The Sunni methodology of belief-first protects Islamic doctrines from being invalidated by flawed proofs, allowing confident use of logic.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the Islamic belief in the existence of angels. According to the Sunni methodology described, would a flawed rational argument for angels (e.g., a weak analogy) affect the truth of that belief? Explain why or why not.
?
Role-play: One person takes the philosophical position (infer first, then believe) and another the Sunni position. Debate a simple theological claim (e.g., 'The Qur'an is the word of God') and show how each methodology handles a failed proof.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
Using Logic Without Adopting its Metaphysics
Author defends the use of logic by distinguishing its method from its metaphysical baggage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how Muslim scholars separated the logical method from its Aristotelian metaphysical assumptions.

Core Idea
You can use a tool without accepting every theory that came with it.

The author begins by acknowledging that Aristotelian logic was both admired and criticized. He points out that Muslim scholars identified problematic metaphysical assumptions in that logic, such as causality between genus and differentia. However, they did not discard logic entirely—they used it as a tool while rejecting its false underpinnings. This lesson explores how they maintained this critical balance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sides of the reception of logic
Find where the author says logic was admired and criticized. Note the phrase 'ولقي إعجاب الكثيرين، وتعرض لنقد الكثيرين أيضا'.
2
Locate the problematic assumptions
Identify the metaphysical issues the author mentions, such as belief in causality between genus and differentia ('كاعتقاد العلية بين الجنس والفصل').
3
Find the author's statement on the widespread use of logic
Locate the sentence beginning with 'ومما اعتاده العلماء المتكلمون' which states that scholars have used logic widely in demonstrating truth and refuting falsehood.
4
Explain the independence of truth from the perfection of logic
Note the author's assertion that 'برد اليقين وصحة المعتقد ليس متوقفا على سلامة المنطق الأرسطي أبدا' (the coolness of certainty is not dependent on the soundness of Aristotelian logic).
This shows the tool is useful but not essential to truth.

ولن يأتي - الفوضويون بمنهج يقاربه، فضلا عما يساويه، فضلا عما هو أحسن منه. وفي اليوم الذي ينبعث المجادلون بما يساويه نجادلهم بالتي هي أحسن مما جاؤوا به، إن شاء الله. وقد يفكر بعض الضعاف لما ذا المنطق؟ والغزالي رحمة الله بين عدم فائدته، وانتهى به الأمر إلى التصوف، وصنف للصوفية أعظم دستور يعتزون به ويسيرون في ضوئه، به إحياء علوم الدين، والوصول إلى اليقين. إن هذا الخاطر قلما ينجو منه طالب؛ حيث الشيطان يراود كل إنسان على حسب طريقته، فالذي يرى صحة مذهب أهل السنة يأتيه الشيطان بمثل هذه الهواجس. فليخبر شيطانه بأن الإمام الغزالي رحمة الله ألف بعد هذا «الإحياء» كتابا كبيرا هو من أعظم الكتب في أصول الفقه، وفي مقدمته تكلم إمام الصوفية هذا في علم المنطق وعنه بكلام سلس رائع، بل فيه قال قولته الشهيرة
Different from Islam and the rational sciences: those methodologies, the most important of which is what we call Aristotelian logic. It received admiration from many and also faced criticism from many. There is no harm in any of that. The imams of Islam also noticed what in this Greek heritage—whether from Aristotle or not—contradicts the beliefs of Islam, and they explained its falseness, and most of that was regarding metaphysical investigations. However, his logic also had a connection to that metaphysics, such as belief in causality between genus and differentia and so on. There has not ceased among us those who point out the corruption of what is corrupt in it. And what the theological scholars have been accustomed to since the early centuries is the use of this type of methodology known as logic, many of whose rules are attributed to Aristotle. Our scholars may agree with him on some and disagree on others, but there is no doubt that this logic has been widely used in demonstrating the correctness of much of what we believe and in refuting the doctrines of the people of falsehood. What the anarchists want when they direct their arrows of criticism at this logic is nothing but the destruction of what this logic has been used for, because they are anarchists, and nothing but to spread... Hence, it is necessary to confront this tribulation with all determination and seriousness. The truth we believe is truth in itself, and our predecessors have established it, and God willing we will establish it before whomever wishes, whoever he may be. The coolness of certainty and soundness of belief is never dependent on the soundness of Aristotelian logic. The falsehood we reject is falsehood in itself, and our scholars have refuted it with the utmost refutation, and by God's permission we are able to do that in any place. Sophistry. From... And our methodology is not to reason first, then believe—that is a philosophical methodology. Rather, we, the community of theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah, believe first and then reason. So if the invalidity of an evidence becomes apparent hypothetically, it does not necessarily mean that the conclusion in itself is false, as long as it is impossible to invalidate the possibility of another evidence for it, whether we know it or not. In light of this possibility, it is impossible to invalidate the soundness of the conclusion, even if another evidence is not presented in the session of debate hypothetically; the conclusion is not invalidated by that, simply because the Ummah has received it with acceptance through the ages, so it is itself the evidence. Nearly seven centuries have passed since the cries to refute logic, yet it has not been refuted, nor has the alternative they desired been established to build upon it a philosophy of tautology. Rather, it has gone from failure to failure. The Ummah did not impose his Sunnah; rather, they rejected his innovation. The adherents of the methodology are still able to demonstrate the soundness of belief before all sects of opponents: polytheists, atheists, materialists, secularists, or various people of innovation. They use logic to achieve this goal, whether they know the points of weakness in it or not, as long as the anarchists have not come—and will not come—with a methodology that approaches it, let alone equals it, let alone is better than it. On the day that arguers come with something equal to it, we will argue with them in the way that is best than what they brought, God willing. And some weak-minded people may think: why logic? Al-Ghazali, may God have mercy on him, showed its lack of benefit, and his end was Sufism, and he authored for the Sufis the greatest constitution they take pride in and follow in its light: 'Ihya Ulum al-Din' and reaching certainty. This thought rarely escapes a student, for Satan tempts every person according to his way. So the one who sees the correctness of the Ahl al-Sunnah school is approached by Satan with such misgivings. Let him inform his Satan that Imam al-Ghazali, may God have mercy on him, after this 'Ihya' authored a great book that is among the greatest books in Usul al-Fiqh, and in its introduction this Imam of Sufism spoke about the science of logic and regarding it with fluid and wonderful speech; indeed, in it he said his famous saying.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter defense of the use of Aristotelian logic in Islamic scholarship. The author begins by acknowledging that Aristotelian logic was admired and criticized, but notes that Muslim scholars identified aspects of Greek philosophy that contradicted Islamic beliefs, especially in metaphysics. However, they continued to use logic itself as a tool for argumentation. The key point is that logic has been widely employed to demonstrate the truth of Islamic beliefs and refute falsehood. The author then attacks 'anarchists' who criticize logic not to correct it but to undermine the conclusions reached through it. He asserts that truth and certainty do not depend on the perfection of Aristotelian logic. The author then distinguishes the methodology of Ahl al-Sunnah: they believe first and then seek evidence, unlike philosophers who reason first. If a particular evidence is invalidated, the belief itself remains valid because there could be other evidence, and the Ummah's consensus suffices as evidence. He then dismisses centuries of criticism against logic, stating that no successful alternative has been provided. The passage ends by addressing a potential objection: Imam al-Ghazali's turn to Sufism and his critique of logic. The author clarifies that al-Ghazali later wrote a major work on Usul al-Fiqh in which he praised logic, thus refuting the idea that he abandoned it entirely.

Key Terms
المنطق الأرسطي
السفسطة
العلية

According to the author, what did Muslim scholars do with Aristotelian logic?
A) Rejected it entirely due to its metaphysical flaws.
B) Adopted it completely, including its metaphysical assumptions.
C) Used it as a methodological tool while rejecting its problematic metaphysics.
D) Ignored it as irrelevant to Islamic theology.

Key Takeaway
Muslim scholars adopted Aristotelian logic as a tool while rejecting its metaphysical baggage, showing that a methodology can be separated from its philosophical origins.

?

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
7 min
Believing First, Reasoning Second
Author explains the epistemological priority of belief over reasoning in Ahl al-Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the epistemological priority of belief over reasoning according to Ahl al-Sunnah.

Core Idea
Certain truth comes from prophetic acceptance, not from syllogistic proof.

The author contrasts the methodology of Ahl al-Sunnah with that of the philosophers. Philosophers reason first and then believe; Ahl al-Sunnah believe first and then reason. This is not anti-rational; it means that if a particular argument fails, the belief remains valid because it is grounded in the Ummah's consensus and the possibility of other proofs. In this lesson, we unpack this powerful epistemological stance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contrasting methodologies
Locate where the author says 'ليس منهجنا هو الاستدلال أولا، ثم الاعتقاد، وهو منهج فلسفي، بل نحن معاشر متكلمي أهل السنة نعتقد أولا ثم نستدل'. Recognize the distinction: philosophers reason then believe, Ahl al-Sunnah believe then reason.
2
Understand the consequence of a failed proof
Find the sentence: 'فإذا تبين بطلان دليل فرضا فإنه لا يعني بالضرورة أن المدلول في حد ذاته باطل'. The author argues that if a proof is invalidated, the conclusion (belief) is not automatically false.
This protects beliefs from being overturned by a single weak argument.
3
Recognize the role of the Ummah's acceptance
Identify the statement: 'فلمجرد أن الأمة تلقته بالقبول عبر العصور، فهو عين الدليل'. The author asserts that the continuous acceptance of a belief by the Ummah is itself a form of evidence.
4
Reflect on why this methodology is epistemologically robust
Consider how this approach safeguards core beliefs from logical critiques. The possibility of other proofs and the weight of tradition prevent belief from being fragile.

Source Text

مختلفة من الإسلام والعلوم العقلية تلك المناهج، من أهمها ما نسميه المنطق الأرسطي، ولقي إعجاب الكثيرين، وتعرض لنقد الكثيرين أيضا. ولا غضاضة في شيء من ذلك. وأئمة الإسلام أيضا تنبهوا إلى ما في هذا التراث اليوناني - سواء هو لأرسطو أو لا - مما يخالف عقائد الإسلام، وبينوا بطلان ذلك، وكان أكثره فيما يتعلق بالمباحث الميتافيزيقية، إلا أن منطقه أيضا كان يمت إلى تلك الميتافيزيقا بصلة، كاعتقاد العلية بين الجنس والفصل وما إلى ذلك، لم يزل فينا من ينبه على فساد الفاسد فيه. ومما اعتاده العلماء المتكلمون منذ القرون استخدام هذا اللون من المنهج المعروف بالمنطق، الكثير من قواعده منسوب إلى أرسطو، قد يوافقه عليه علمائنا وقد يخالفونه إلا أن مما لا شك فيه أن هذا المنطق استخدم استخداما عريضا في بيان صحة كثير مما نعتقده، وإبطالِ مذاهب أهل الباطل. والذي يريده الفوضويون حين يوجهون سهام النقد إلى هذا المنطق ليس إلا هدم ما استخدم فيه هذا المنطق؛ لأنهم فوضويون، وليس إلا نشر ومن هنا يجب التصدي لهذه الفتنة بكل عزم وجدية، والحق الذي نعتقده حق في نفسه، وقد أثبته سلفنا، وإن شاء الله سنثبته عند من يريد، كائنا كان، وبرد اليقين وصحة المعتقد ليس متوقفا على سلامة المنطق الأرسطي أبدا، والباطل الذي نرفضه باطل في نفسه، وقد أبطله علمائنا شر إبطال، وبإذن الله نقدر على ذلك في أي مكان كان. السفسطة. من وليس منهجنا هو الاستدلال أولا، ثم الاعتقاد، وهو منهج فلسفي، بل نحن معاشر متكلمي أهل السنة نعتقد أولا ثم نستدل، فإذا تبين بطلان دليل فرضا فإنه لا يعني بالضرورة أن المدلول في حد ذاته باطل، طالما يستحيل إبطال احتمال وجود دليل آخر عليه عرفناه أو لم نعرفه، ففي ظل هذا الاحتمال استحال إبطال صحة المدلول، حتى وإن لم يتم إقامة دليل آخر عليه في مجلس المناظرة فرضا فلا ينتقض المدلول بذلك؛ لمجرد أن الأمة تلقته بالقبول عبر العصور، فهو عين الدليل. لقد مضى على صيحات نقض المنطق ما يقرب من سبعة قرون، إلا أنه لم ينتقض بعد، ولم تتم إقامة بديل أراده ليشيد فوقه فلسفة الحشو، بل هو من فشل إلى فشل، لم يفرض الأمةُ سُنَّته، بل رفضوا بدعته. وأصحاب المنهج ما زالوا متمكنين من بيان صحة المعتقد أمام كل طوائف المخالفين، وثنيين، أو ملحدين، أو ماديين أو دهريين أو علمانيين، أو أهل بدعة مختلفين. يستخدمون المنطق في تحقيق هذا الهدف، علموا مواضع الخلل فيه أو لم يعلموا، طالما لم يأت - ولن يأتي - الفوضويون بمنهج يقاربه، فضلا عما يساويه، فضلا عما هو أحسن منه. وفي اليوم الذي ينبعث المجادلون بما يساويه نجادلهم بالتي هي أحسن مما جاؤوا به، إن شاء الله. وقد يفكر بعض الضعاف لما ذا المنطق؟ والغزالي رحمة الله بين عدم فائدته، وانتهى به الأمر إلى التصوف، وصنف للصوفية أعظم دستور يعتزون به ويسيرون في ضوئه، به إحياء علوم الدين، والوصول إلى اليقين. إن هذا الخاطر قلما ينجو منه طالب؛ حيث الشيطان يراود كل إنسان على حسب طريقته، فالذي يرى صحة مذهب أهل السنة يأتيه الشيطان بمثل هذه الهواجس. فليخبر شيطانه بأن الإمام الغزالي رحمة الله ألف بعد هذا «الإحياء» كتابا كبيرا هو من أعظم الكتب في أصول الفقه، وفي مقدمته تكلم إمام الصوفية هذا في علم المنطق وعنه بكلام سلس رائع، بل فيه قال قولته الشهيرة
Different from Islam and the rational sciences: those methodologies, the most important of which is what we call Aristotelian logic. It received admiration from many and also faced criticism from many. There is no harm in any of that. The imams of Islam also noticed what in this Greek heritage—whether from Aristotle or not—contradicts the beliefs of Islam, and they explained its falseness, and most of that was regarding metaphysical investigations. However, his logic also had a connection to that metaphysics, such as belief in causality between genus and differentia and so on. There has not ceased among us those who point out the corruption of what is corrupt in it. And what the theological scholars have been accustomed to since the early centuries is the use of this type of methodology known as logic, many of whose rules are attributed to Aristotle. Our scholars may agree with him on some and disagree on others, but there is no doubt that this logic has been widely used in demonstrating the correctness of much of what we believe and in refuting the doctrines of the people of falsehood. What the anarchists want when they direct their arrows of criticism at this logic is nothing but the destruction of what this logic has been used for, because they are anarchists, and nothing but to spread... Hence, it is necessary to confront this tribulation with all determination and seriousness. The truth we believe is truth in itself, and our predecessors have established it, and God willing we will establish it before whomever wishes, whoever he may be. The coolness of certainty and soundness of belief is never dependent on the soundness of Aristotelian logic. The falsehood we reject is falsehood in itself, and our scholars have refuted it with the utmost refutation, and by God's permission we are able to do that in any place. Sophistry. From... And our methodology is not to reason first, then believe—that is a philosophical methodology. Rather, we, the community of theologians of Ahl al-Sunnah, believe first and then reason. So if the invalidity of an evidence becomes apparent hypothetically, it does not necessarily mean that the conclusion in itself is false, as long as it is impossible to invalidate the possibility of another evidence for it, whether we know it or not. In light of this possibility, it is impossible to invalidate the soundness of the conclusion, even if another evidence is not presented in the session of debate hypothetically; the conclusion is not invalidated by that, simply because the Ummah has received it with acceptance through the ages, so it is itself the evidence. Nearly seven centuries have passed since the cries to refute logic, yet it has not been refuted, nor has the alternative they desired been established to build upon it a philosophy of tautology. Rather, it has gone from failure to failure. The Ummah did not impose his Sunnah; rather, they rejected his innovation. The adherents of the methodology are still able to demonstrate the soundness of belief before all sects of opponents: polytheists, atheists, materialists, secularists, or various people of innovation. They use logic to achieve this goal, whether they know the points of weakness in it or not, as long as the anarchists have not come—and will not come—with a methodology that approaches it, let alone equals it, let alone is better than it. On the day that arguers come with something equal to it, we will argue with them in the way that is best than what they brought, God willing. And some weak-minded people may think: why logic? Al-Ghazali, may God have mercy on him, showed its lack of benefit, and his end was Sufism, and he authored for the Sufis the greatest constitution they take pride in and follow in its light: 'Ihya Ulum al-Din' and reaching certainty. This thought rarely escapes a student, for Satan tempts every person according to his way. So the one who sees the correctness of the Ahl al-Sunnah school is approached by Satan with such misgivings. Let him inform his Satan that Imam al-Ghazali, may God have mercy on him, after this 'Ihya' authored a great book that is among the greatest books in Usul al-Fiqh, and in its introduction this Imam of Sufism spoke about the science of logic and regarding it with fluid and wonderful speech; indeed, in it he said his famous saying.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter defense of the use of Aristotelian logic in Islamic scholarship. The author begins by acknowledging that Aristotelian logic was admired and criticized, but notes that Muslim scholars identified aspects of Greek philosophy that contradicted Islamic beliefs, especially in metaphysics. However, they continued to use logic itself as a tool for argumentation. The key point is that logic has been widely employed to demonstrate the truth of Islamic beliefs and refute falsehood. The author then attacks 'anarchists' who criticize logic not to correct it but to undermine the conclusions reached through it. He asserts that truth and certainty do not depend on the perfection of Aristotelian logic. The author then distinguishes the methodology of Ahl al-Sunnah: they believe first and then seek evidence, unlike philosophers who reason first. If a particular evidence is invalidated, the belief itself remains valid because there could be other evidence, and the Ummah's consensus suffices as evidence. He then dismisses centuries of criticism against logic, stating that no successful alternative has been provided. The passage ends by addressing a potential objection: Imam al-Ghazali's turn to Sufism and his critique of logic. The author clarifies that al-Ghazali later wrote a major work on Usul al-Fiqh in which he praised logic, thus refuting the idea that he abandoned it entirely.

Key Terms
المنطق الأرسطي
السفسطة
العلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what happens if a proof for a belief is invalidated in a debate?
A) The belief itself becomes invalid.
B) The belief remains valid because the Ummah's acceptance serves as evidence.
C) The belief must be immediately abandoned until a new proof is found.
D) The belief is only valid if the proof is logically sound.

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunnah believe first and then reason, ensuring that core beliefs are not fragilely dependent on any single logical argument.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Take a core Islamic belief (e.g., the necessity of prayer). Construct a possible logical objection against it. Then apply the author's principle to show why that objection does not invalidate the belief.
?

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
10 min
Logic as the Foundation of All Sciences
Author establishes logic as foundation of all sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why logic is considered the foundational science (muqaddima) for all Islamic sciences, using the author's arguments.

Core Idea
Logic is the gatekeeper of all knowledge; without it, no science can be trusted.

The author begins by declaring that logic is the introduction to all sciences, quoting al-Ghazali. He insists that one who lacks logical knowledge cannot be trusted even in his own specialty. This lesson explores why logic holds this foundational role and how it relates to other Islamic disciplines.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Author's Claim
Look for the phrase 'مقدمة العلوم كلها'. The author asserts logic is the preface to all sciences. Think about what that means: logic provides the tools for reasoning in any discipline.
2
Find the Consequence of Ignorance
The author says 'لا ثقة له بعلومه أصلا' — no confidence in his sciences. So logic is not optional; it validates all other knowledge.
3
Understand the Process of Development
The author mentions that earlier scholars added and deleted from logic, and later scholars critiqued them. This shows that logic itself is subject to development, but only by qualified scholars.
4
Relate to Islamic Sciences
Logic is used in kalam (theology), usul al-fiqh (jurisprudence), and tafsir (exegesis) to structure arguments and ensure validity. Think of a specific argument from these fields.
Example: In kalam, the proof of the world's temporality often uses a categorical syllogism.
