Understanding Commentary Genres in Islamic Logic
Lists the author's major works and their genres.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a sharh, a hashiya, and a munhiya in the Islamic logical tradition based on their functions and relationships.

Core Idea
Knowing the genre of a work tells you its place in the commentary hierarchy.

In this passage, the author lists his own scholarly works, including a sharh (commentary), a munhiyat (critical notes), and a hashiya (gloss). These terms are not just names but indicate the type of scholarly engagement. Understanding these categories helps you navigate the vast literature of Islamic logic and identify the primary source, its explanation, and the refinements added by later scholars.

Guided Path
1
Locate the three works in the Arabic list.
Find the numbers 1, 2, 3 and read the titles of the works. This gives you concrete examples of each genre.
The list is: 1. Sharh Sullam al-Ulum, 2. al-Munhiyat, 3. Hāshiya.
2
Identify the base work (matn) for each commentary.
For the sharh, the matn is Sullam al-Ulum. For the munhiyat, the base is Bahr al-Ulum's own sharh. For the hashiya, the base is Mir Zahid's treatise.
The munhiyat is a commentary on a commentary, making it a second-level work.
3
Understand the hierarchy of commentary genres.
The typical hierarchy is: matn (original) → sharh (explanation) → hashiya (gloss) or munhiyat (critical notes). Each layer adds more analysis or critique.
A munhiyat often evaluates and completes the sharh, while a hashiya provides marginal notes.
4
Apply the hierarchy to a real Islamic logic curriculum.
Think of Sullam al-Ulum as the foundational text in logic. Its sharh by Bahr al-Ulum is the main commentary, and students might consult the munhiyat for deeper critique or the hashiya for clarifications.
Knowing this helps you choose the right level of reading for your study.

The third section: His writings and scholarly works
He is considered Allamah Bahr al-Ulum from the great authors in the Islamic world, and from the famous authors in the Indian lands. His concern was not limited to merely reading others, but he was very keen on authorship and writing. He was given in the art of composing strong skill and great experience that makes his memory lasting over time; he left dozens of works, large, small, and medium, in various branches of knowledge and learning, especially the intellectual and philosophical sciences. These works are admired by researchers and scholars since their publication until now; the people of knowledge have paid attention to them by reading and teaching, and they have published them in the regions of the Islamic world, printed or manuscript. A quick glance at that enormous scientific wealth tells us of the greatness of the man and the country in which he lived. Here are some of what our humble research has reached in praise of this blessed scientific heritage:
1. Sharh Sullam al-Ulum in Logic, and this is what I am producing today. It is among his earliest works; he said in its conclusion: 'I composed it in the prime of youth and the first bloom of the core of life.' He referred to it in several places from 'Fawatih al-Rahmut'.
2. Al-Munhiyat on his commentary on Sullam al-Ulum.
3. A gloss on Mir Zahid's treatise in logic, printed - and printed with it on the margin Kashf al-Maktum and al-Qawl al-Muhil, both by Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Lakhnawi, in Delhi/India, year 1292 AH/1875 CE, in 66 pages, lithographic print. And also printed... (footnotes omitted)
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a front matter section that introduces the author's scholarly output, particularly focusing on his commentary on Sullam al-Ulum, which is the work being edited in this book. The author, Allamah Bahr al-Ulum, is described as a prolific writer who authored dozens of works in various fields, especially in rational and philosophical sciences. His works are highly regarded and have been widely studied and published. The text lists three specific works: first, his Sharh Sullam al-Ulum on logic, which he composed in his youth and is the subject of the present edition. Second, al-Munhiyat, which is a critical commentary on his own Sharh. Third, a gloss (hāshiya) on Mir Zahid's treatise on logic, which was published with other works on the margin. This listing shows the author's deep engagement with logical studies and his contribution to the field.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Importance of Sullam al-Ulum and the Decline of Logic Study
Introduces the book and the decline of logic study

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the historical context and significance of Bahr Ulum's commentary on Sullam al-Ulum, and identify the causes of educational decline in logic as outlined in the introduction.

Core Idea
Books have biographies: Sullam al-Ulum, though not the oldest, lived long and guided many.

This passage opens Bahr Ulum's commentary on Sullam al-Ulum, a standard logic textbook. The author uses the metaphor of a book's life to emphasize its enduring impact. He then laments the decline of logic study in India, contrasting past thoroughness with present scarcity. Understanding this context helps us appreciate why this commentary was written and why reviving such texts is crucial for Islamic education today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's purpose
The passage is an introduction (ta'rif) to the book. Bahr Ulum aims to reintroduce Sullam al-Ulum to scholars because it is important yet neglected. He begins by comparing a book's life to that of a person — some die early, some live long. He asserts that Sullam, though not the oldest, surpasses older books in impact.
The term 'ta'rif' here means acquainting the reader with the book, not logical definition.
2
Trace the decline described
The author highlights the decline of logic study in India: previously, students read advanced commentaries like Yazdi on Tahdhib, Qutb al-Razi on Shamsiyya, and three commentaries on Sullam. Now, very few can complete Yazdi. Moreover, these books are unavailable in markets, making it hard for new students to acquire them.
Note the three stages of decline: inability to finish earlier texts, low readership, and unavailability of books.
3
Connect to the book's significance
Despite older books, Sullam al-Ulum has greater impact and direction for ideas. The decline makes this commentary necessary to re-engage scholars. The author's motivational tone stresses the urgency of reviving the study of this text.
This introduction sets the stage for the commentary, explaining why it was written.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شرح بحر العلوم على سلم العلوم الفصل الثاني تعريف بكتاب «شرح سلّم العلوم» تمهید للكتب تاريخ كتاريخ الأشخاص، وحياة لا تخلو من صعود وهبوط، ورب كتاب يولد ميتا، وآخر تقدر له حياة طويلة عريضة، وكتاب «السلم» وإن كان هناك كتب أسن منه ، ولكنه يزيد عليها تأثيرا وتوجيها للأفكار. إن كتاب «سلم العلوم» رغم كل ما له من الأهمية، بحاجة إلى التعريف به لأهل العلم في العالم الإسلامي، سواء في ذلك الهند وغير الهند. أما الهند فقد انحط النشاط الدراسي في مدارسها وجامعاتها إلى درجة متدنية في هذه الآونة الأخيرة، بحيث لا نجد فيها من يصبر على تمام قراءة شرح اليزدي على التهذيب إلا قليلا جدا ، بعد أن كان الأسلاف يقرؤونه كاملا ثم يواصلون دراسة المنطق في شرح القطب الرازي على الشمسية، وبعده يقرؤون في ثلاثة شروح للسلم . ومن مظاهر هذا الانحطاط أن لا يتوفر مثل هذه الكتب في الأسواق للشراء، حتى إذا أراد أحد أن يدرسها ، أو يقتني نسخة منها على الأقل فليس بمُكْنَته شراؤها وتملكها، وذلك بعد أن مضى حين من الدهر كانت الأسواق
The explanation of Bahr Ulum on Sullam al-Ulum. Chapter two: Introduction to the book 'Sharh Sullam al-Ulum'. Preamble: Books have a history like the history of people, and a life not free from rise and fall. Perhaps a book is born dead, and another is destined for a long and broad life. The book 'al-Sullam', although there are older books, surpasses them in impact and direction of ideas. Indeed, the book 'Sullam al-Ulum', despite all its importance, needs to be introduced to scholars in the Islamic world, both in India and elsewhere. As for India, academic activity in its schools and universities has declined to a low degree recently, to the extent that we find very few who can bear to completely read the commentary of Yazdi on al-Tahdhib, whereas the predecessors used to read it fully and then continue studying logic in the commentary of Qutb al-Razi on al-Shamsiyya, and after that they would read three commentaries on al-Sullam. Among the manifestations of this decline is that such books are not available in the markets for purchase, so if someone wants to study them or at least acquire a copy, they cannot buy and own them, after a time had passed when the markets [were full].
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is an introduction to the book Sharh Sullam al-Ulum. It begins with a comparison: books have lives like people, some die early, some live long. The author asserts that Sullam al-Ulum, though not the oldest, has greater impact and direction for ideas. Then it explains the need to introduce this book to scholars, especially in India where educational standards have declined. Previously, students would read advanced logic texts like Yazdi's commentary on Tahdhib and Qutb al-Razi's commentary on Shamsiyya, followed by three commentaries on Sullam. Now, few can even complete the Yazdi commentary. Moreover, such books are unavailable in markets, making it hard for new students to acquire them. This highlights the sad state of learning and the importance of reviving the study of this book.

Key Terms
سلم العلوم (Sullam al-Ulum): a standard logic textbook
التعريف (al-ta'rif): introduction, here meaning acquainting scholars with the book

Key Takeaway
